</table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        West Virginia\n       </b>\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">\n         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">\n          /\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="/\xcb\x8c/: secondary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x8c\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'w\' in \'wind\'">\n            w\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x9b/: \'e\' in \'dress\'">\n            \xc9\x9b\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'s\' in \'sigh\'">\n            s\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'t\' in \'tie\'">\n            t\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">\n           <span title="\'v\' in \'vie\'">\n            v\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99r/: \'er\' in \'letter\'">\n            \xc9\x99r\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\n            \xcb\x88\n           </span>\n           <span title="/d\xca\x92/: \'j\' in \'jam\'">\n            d\xca\x92\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\xaa/: \'i\' in \'kit\'">\n            \xc9\xaa\n           </span>\n           <span title="\'n\' in \'nigh\'">\n            n\n           </span>\n           <span title="/j/: \'y\' in \'yes\'">\n            j\n           </span>\n           <span title="/\xc9\x99/: \'a\' in \'about\'">\n            \xc9\x99\n           </span>\n          </span>\n          /\n         </a>\n        </span>\n        <small class="nowrap">\n         (\n         <span class="unicode haudio">\n          <span class="fn">\n           <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n            <a href="/wiki/File:En-us-West_Virginia.ogg" title="About this sound">\n             <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>\n            </a>\n           </span>\n           <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ad/En-us-West_Virginia.ogg" title="En-us-West Virginia.ogg">\n            listen\n           </a>\n          </span>\n         </span>\n         )\n        </small>\n       </span>\n       is a\n       <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">\n        state\n       </a>\n       located in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">\n        Appalachian\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Region" title="Region">\n        region\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        Southern\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geography.vt.edu_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-geography.vt.edu-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n        <a href="#cite_note-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It is bordered by\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       to the southeast,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       to the southwest,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       to the northwest,\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       to the north (and, slightly, east), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       to the northeast. West Virginia is the\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">\n        10th smallest by area\n       </a>\n       , is\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">\n        ranked 38th in population\n       </a>\n       , and has the second lowest\n       <a href="/wiki/Household_income_in_the_United_States#Income_by_state" title="Household income in the United States">\n        household income\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states" title="List of U.S. states">\n        50 United States\n       </a>\n       . The capital and largest city is\n       <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_West_Virginia" title="Charleston, West Virginia">\n        Charleston\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia became a state following the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheeling_Convention" title="Wheeling Convention">\n        Wheeling Conventions\n       </a>\n       of 1861, after the American\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n        Civil War\n       </a>\n       had begun. Delegates from some Unionist counties of northwestern Virginia decided to\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="West Virginia in the American Civil War">\n        break away\n       </a>\n       from\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       , although they included many secessionist counties in the new state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia was admitted to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">\n        Union\n       </a>\n       on June 20, 1863, and was a key\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Border_states_(Civil_War)" title="Border states (Civil War)">\n        border state\n       </a>\n       during the war. West Virginia was the only state to form by separating from a\n       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">\n        Confederate\n       </a>\n       state, the first to separate from any state since\n       <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">\n        Maine\n       </a>\n       separated from\n       <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts" title="Massachusetts">\n        Massachusetts\n       </a>\n       , and was one of two states admitted to the Union during the American Civil War (the other being\n       <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">\n        Nevada\n       </a>\n       ). While a portion of its residents held slaves, most of the residents were yeomen farmers, and the delegates provided for gradual abolition of slavery in the new state constitution.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Geographers" title="Association of American Geographers">\n        Association of American Geographers\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-geography.vt.edu_7-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-geography.vt.edu-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       classify West Virginia as part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        Southern United States\n       </a>\n       . The northern panhandle extends adjacent to Pennsylvania and Ohio, with the West Virginia cities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheeling,_West_Virginia" title="Wheeling, West Virginia">\n        Wheeling\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Weirton,_West_Virginia" title="Weirton, West Virginia">\n        Weirton\n       </a>\n       just across the border from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">\n        Pittsburgh\n       </a>\n       metropolitan area, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Bluefield,_West_Virginia" title="Bluefield, West Virginia">\n        Bluefield\n       </a>\n       is less than 70 miles (110\xc2\xa0km) from\n       <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">\n        North Carolina\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_West_Virginia" title="Huntington, West Virginia">\n        Huntington\n       </a>\n       in the southwest is close to the states of Ohio and Kentucky, while\n       <a href="/wiki/Martinsburg,_West_Virginia" title="Martinsburg, West Virginia">\n        Martinsburg\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harpers_Ferry" title="Harpers Ferry">\n        Harpers Ferry\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Panhandle" title="Eastern Panhandle">\n        Eastern Panhandle\n       </a>\n       region are considered part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">\n        Washington\n       </a>\n       metropolitan area, in between the states of Maryland and Virginia. The unique position of West Virginia means that it is often included in several geographical regions, including the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_states" title="Mid-Atlantic states">\n        Mid-Atlantic\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Upland_South" title="Upland South">\n        Upland South\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">\n        Southeastern United States\n       </a>\n       . It is the only state that is entirely within the area served by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Regional_Commission" title="Appalachian Regional Commission">\n        Appalachian Regional Commission\n       </a>\n       ; the area is commonly defined as "\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachia" title="Appalachia">\n        Appalachia\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARC_service_area_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ARC_service_area-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state is noted for its mountains and rolling hills, its historically significant\n       <a href="/wiki/Logging" title="Logging">\n        logging\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining" title="Coal mining">\n        coal mining\n       </a>\n       industries, and its political and\n       <a href="/wiki/Labor_history_(discipline)" title="Labor history (discipline)">\n        labor history\n       </a>\n       . It is one of the most densely\n       <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">\n        karstic\n       </a>\n       areas in the world, making it a choice area for recreational caving and scientific research.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources in the body of the article. (April 2016)">\n           not verified in body\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The karst lands contribute to much of the state\'s cool trout waters.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources in the body of the article. (April 2016)">\n           not verified in body\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       It is also known for a wide range of outdoor recreational opportunities, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">\n        skiing\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whitewater_rafting" title="Whitewater rafting">\n        whitewater rafting\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">\n        fishing\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">\n        hiking\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Backpacking_(wilderness)" title="Backpacking (wilderness)">\n        backpacking\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Mountain_biking" title="Mountain biking">\n        mountain biking\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">\n        rock climbing\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">\n        hunting\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div  </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41">\n           <a href="#Colleges_and_universities">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             9.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Colleges and universities\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48">\n           <a href="#Literature">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             10.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Literature\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49">\n           <a href="#In_popular_culture">\n            <span        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50">\n         <a href="#See_also">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           11\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-52">\n         <a href="#Further_reading">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Further reading\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-53">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_West_Virginia" title="History of West Virginia">\n        History of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Many ancient man-made earthen mounds from various prehistoric\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mound_builder_(people)" title="Mound builder (people)">\n        mound builder cultures\n       </a>\n       survive, especially in the areas of present-day\n       <a href="/wiki/Moundsville,_West_Virginia" title="Moundsville, West Virginia">\n        Moundsville\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Charleston,_West_Virginia" title="South Charleston, West Virginia">\n        South Charleston\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Romney,_West_Virginia" title="Romney, West Virginia">\n        Romney\n       </a>\n       . The artifacts uncovered in these give evidence of village societies. They had a tribal trade system culture that crafted\n       <a href="/wiki/Work_hardening" title="Work hardening">\n        cold-worked\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">\n        copper\n       </a>\n       pieces.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the 1670s during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Beaver_Wars" title="Beaver Wars">\n        Beaver Wars\n       </a>\n       , the powerful\n       <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">\n        Iroquois\n       </a>\n       , five allied nations based in present-day New York and Pennsylvania, drove out other American Indian tribes from the region in order to reserve the upper Ohio Valley as a hunting ground.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siouan_language" title="Siouan language">\n        Siouan language\n       </a>\n       tribes, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Moneton" title="Moneton">\n        Moneton\n       </a>\n       , had previously been recorded in the area.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A century later, the area now identified as West Virginia was contested territory among Anglo-Americans as well, with the colonies of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       claiming territorial rights under their colonial charters to this area before the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       . Some speculative land companies, such as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vandalia_Company" title="Vandalia Company">\n        Vandalia Company\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and later the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Company" title="Ohio Company">\n        Ohio Company\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indiana_Company" title="Indiana Company">\n        Indiana Company\n       </a>\n       , tried to legitimize their claims to land in parts of West Virginia and Kentucky, but failed. With the federal settlement of the Pennsylvania and Virginia border dispute, which resulted in the creation of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       , Kentuckians "were satisfied [...], and the inhabitants of a large part of West Virginia were grateful."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Crown considered the area of West Virginia to be part of the British\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Colony" title="Virginia Colony">\n        Virginia Colony\n       </a>\n       from 1607 to 1776. The United States considered this area to be the western part of the state of\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       (which was commonly referred as\n       <i>\n        Trans-Allegheny Virginia\n       </i>\n       ) from 1776 to 1863, before the formation of West Virginia. Its residents were discontented for years with their position in Virginia, as the government was dominated by the planter elite of the Tidewater and Piedmont areas. The legislature had electoral malapportionment, based on the counting of slaves toward regional populations, and the western white residents were underrepresented in the state legislature. More subsistence and yeoman farmers lived in the west and they were generally less supportive of slavery, although many counties were divided on their support. The residents of this area became more sharply divided after the planter elite of eastern Virginia voted to secede from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">\n        Union\n       </a>\n       during the Civil War.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Residents of the western and northern counties set up a separate government under Francis Pierpont in 1861, which they called the\n       <a href="/wiki/Restored_Government_of_Virginia" title="Restored Government of Virginia">\n        Restored Government\n       </a>\n       . Most voted to separate from Virginia, and the new state was admitted to the Union in 1863. In 1864 a state constitutional convention drafted a constitution, which was ratified by the legislature without putting it to popular vote. West Virginia abolished\n       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">\n        slavery\n       </a>\n       by a gradual process and temporarily\n       <a href="/wiki/Disfranchisement" title="Disfranchisement">\n        disenfranchised\n       </a>\n       men who had held Confederate office or fought for the Confederacy.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia\'s history has been profoundly affected by its mountainous terrain, numerous and vast river valleys, and rich natural resources. These were all factors driving its economy and the lifestyles of its residents, who tended to live in many small, relatively isolated communities in the mountain valleys. Geography continues to be important to the state.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">\n        Prehistory\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Prehistory">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       For more details on this topic, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_West_Virginia" title="Prehistory of West Virginia">\n        Prehistory of West Virginia\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Protohistory_of_West_Virginia" title="Protohistory of West Virginia">\n        Protohistory of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A 2010 analysis of a local\n       <a href="/wiki/Stalagmite" title="Stalagmite">\n        stalagmite\n       </a>\n       revealed that Native Americans were burning forests to clear land as early as 100\n       <span class="nowrap">\n       </span>\n       BC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some regional late-prehistoric\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Woodland" title="Eastern Woodland">\n        Eastern Woodland\n       </a>\n       tribes were more involved in hunting and fishing, practicing the slash-and-burn\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Agricultural_Complex" title="Eastern Agricultural Complex">\n        Eastern Agricultural Complex\n       </a>\n       gardening method, which used fire to clear out underbrush from certain area.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (May 2011)">\n           clarification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Another group progressed to the more time-consuming, advanced companion crop fields method of gardening. Also continuing from ancient\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_people" title="Indigenous people">\n        indigenous people\n       </a>\n       of the state, they cultivated\n       <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">\n        tobacco\n       </a>\n       through to early historic times. It was used in numerous social and religious rituals.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       "\n       <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">\n        Maize\n       </a>\n       (corn) did not make a substantial contribution to the diet until after 1150\n       <a href="/wiki/Before_Present" title="Before Present">\n        BP\n       </a>\n       ", to quote Mills (OSU 2003)\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#What_information_to_include" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">\n          <span title="A more detailed citation is required. (August 2016)">\n           full citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       . Eventually, tribal villages began depending on corn to feed their\n       <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">\n        turkey\n       </a>\n       flocks, as Kanawha Fort Ancients practiced bird\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Husbandry" title="Husbandry">\n        husbandry\n       </a>\n       . The local Indians made corn bread and a flat rye bread called "banick" as they emerged from the protohistoric era. A horizon extending from a little before the early 18th century is sometimes called the acculturating\n       <i>\n        Fireside Cabin culture\n       </i>\n       . Trading posts were established by European traders along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">\n        Potomac\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/James_River" title="James River">\n        James rivers\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tribes which inhabited West Virginia as of the 16th century were the Calicua\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in the north, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Susquehannock" title="Susquehannock">\n        Susquehannock\n       </a>\n       in the area immediately south of western Maryland, &amp; the Hokan Sioux (Ancestral Sioux) tribes known as the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saponi" title="Saponi">\n        Saponi\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Moneton" title="Moneton">\n        Moneton\n       </a>\n       &amp;\n       <a href="/wiki/Tutelo" title="Tutelo">\n        Tutelo\n       </a>\n       (situated east-west).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Tribes which came to inhabit West Virginia afterward were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">\n        Shawnee\n       </a>\n       &amp; Kentatentonga Iroquois,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       who fractured off of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Petun" title="Petun">\n        Petun\n       </a>\n       to the north. They were also known as the Gwiandotte.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="European_exploration_and_settlement">\n        European exploration and settlement\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: European exploration and settlement">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Vandalia_(colony)" title="Vandalia (colony)">\n        Vandalia (colony)\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Westsylvania" title="Westsylvania">\n        Westsylvania\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ThomasLEE.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="257" data-file-width="198" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/ThomasLEE.JPG/170px-ThomasLEE.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/95/ThomasLEE.JPG 1.5x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ThomasLEE.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Lee_(Virginia_colonist)" title="Thomas Lee (Virginia colonist)">\n          Thomas Lee\n         </a>\n         , the first manager of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Company" title="Ohio Company">\n          Ohio Company\n         </a>\n         of Virginia.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 1671, General\n       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Wood" title="Abraham Wood">\n        Abraham Wood\n       </a>\n       , at the direction of Royal Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Berkeley_(governor)" title="William Berkeley (governor)">\n        William Berkeley\n       </a>\n       of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Colony" title="Virginia Colony">\n        Virginia Colony\n       </a>\n       , sent a party from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fort_Henry,_Virginia" title="Fort Henry, Virginia">\n        Fort Henry\n       </a>\n       led by Thomas Batts and Robert Fallam to survey this territory. They were the first Europeans recorded as discovering\n       <a href="/wiki/Glen_Ferris,_West_Virginia" title="Glen Ferris, West Virginia">\n        Kanawha Falls\n       </a>\n       . Some sources state that Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Spotswood" title="Alexander Spotswood">\n        Alexander Spotswood\n       </a>\n       \'s 1716\n       <a href="/wiki/Knights_of_the_Golden_Horseshoe_Expedition" title="Knights of the Golden Horseshoe Expedition">\n        Knights of the Golden Horseshoe Expedition\n       </a>\n       (for which the state\'s Golden Horseshoe Competition for 8th graders was named) had penetrated as far as\n       <a href="/wiki/Pendleton_County,_West_Virginia" title="Pendleton County, West Virginia">\n        Pendleton County\n       </a>\n       ; however, modern historians interpret the original accounts of the excursion as suggesting that none of the expedition\'s horsemen ventured much farther west of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">\n        Blue Ridge Mountains\n       </a>\n       than\n       <a href="/wiki/Harrisonburg,_Virginia" title="Harrisonburg, Virginia">\n        Harrisonburg, Virginia\n       </a>\n       . John Van Metre, an Indian trader, penetrated into the northern portion in 1725. The same year,\n       <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">\n        German\n       </a>\n       settlers from\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">\n        Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       founded New Mecklenburg, the present\n       <a href="/wiki/Shepherdstown,_West_Virginia" title="Shepherdstown, West Virginia">\n        Shepherdstown\n       </a>\n       , on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Potomac_River" title="Potomac River">\n        Potomac River\n       </a>\n       , and others followed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       King\n       <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">\n        Charles II of England\n       </a>\n       , in 1661, granted to a company of gentlemen the land between the Potomac and\n       <a href="/wiki/Rappahannock_River" title="Rappahannock River">\n        Rappahannock\n       </a>\n       rivers, known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Neck" title="Northern Neck">\n        Northern Neck\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fairfax,_6th_Lord_Fairfax_of_Cameron" title="Thomas Fairfax, 6th Lord Fairfax of Cameron">\n        Thomas Fairfax, 6th Lord Fairfax of Cameron\n       </a>\n       ultimately took possession of this grant, and in 1746, a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fairfax_Stone" title="Fairfax Stone">\n        stone\n       </a>\n       was erected at the source of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Branch_Potomac_River" title="North Branch Potomac River">\n        North Branch Potomac River\n       </a>\n       to mark the western limit of his grant. A considerable part of this land was surveyed by the young\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">\n        George Washington\n       </a>\n       between 1748 and 1751. The diary kept by Washington recorded that there were already many squatters, largely of German origin, along the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Branch_Potomac_River" title="South Branch Potomac River">\n        South Branch Potomac River\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Gist" title="Christopher Gist">\n        Christopher Gist\n       </a>\n       , a surveyor in the employ of the first\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Company" title="Ohio Company">\n        Ohio Company\n       </a>\n       , which was composed chiefly of Virginians, explored the country along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">\n        Ohio River\n       </a>\n       north of the mouth of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kanawha_River" title="Kanawha River">\n        Kanawha River\n       </a>\n       between 1751 and 1752. The company sought to have a fourteenth colony established with the name "\n       <a href="/wiki/Vandalia_(colony)" title="Vandalia (colony)">\n        Vandalia\n       </a>\n       ". Many settlers crossed the mountains after 1750, though they were hindered by Native American resistance. Few Native Americans lived permanently within the present limits of the state, but the region was a common hunting ground, crossed by many trails. During the\n       <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">\n        French and Indian War\n       </a>\n       (the North American front of the Seven Years\' War in Europe), Indian allies of the French nearly destroyed the scattered British settlements.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Shortly before the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       , in 1774 the Crown Governor of Virginia\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Murray,_4th_Earl_of_Dunmore" title="John Murray, 4th Earl of Dunmore">\n        John Murray, 4th Earl of Dunmore\n       </a>\n       , led a force over the mountains. A body of militia under\n       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Lewis_(soldier)" title="Andrew Lewis (soldier)">\n        then-Colonel Andrew Lewis\n       </a>\n       dealt the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shawnee_Indians" title="Shawnee Indians">\n        Shawnee Indians\n       </a>\n       , under\n       <a href="/wiki/Cornstalk" title="Cornstalk">\n        Hokoleskwa\n       </a>\n       (or "Cornstalk"), a crushing blow during the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Point_Pleasant" title="Battle of Point Pleasant">\n        Battle of Point Pleasant\n       </a>\n       at the junction of the Kanawha and the Ohio rivers. At the Treaty of Camp Charlotte concluding\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dunmore%27s_War" title="Dunmore\'s War">\n        Dunmore\'s War\n       </a>\n       , Cornstalk agreed to recognize the Ohio River as the new boundary with the "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_Knives" title="Long Knives">\n        Long Knives\n       </a>\n       ". By 1776, however, the Shawnee had returned to war, joining the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chickamauga_Cherokee" title="Chickamauga Cherokee">\n        Chickamauga\n       </a>\n       , a band of\n       <a href="/wiki/Cherokee" title="Cherokee">\n        Cherokee\n       </a>\n       known for the area where they lived. Native American attacks on settlers continued until after the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">\n        American Revolutionary War\n       </a>\n       . During the war, the settlers in western Virginia were generally active Whigs and many served in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Continental_Army" title="Continental Army">\n        Continental Army\n       </a>\n       . However,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Claypool%27s_Rebellion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Claypool\'s Rebellion (page does not exist)">\n        Claypool\'s Rebellion\n       </a>\n       of 1780\xe2\x80\x931781, in which a group of men refused to pay taxes imposed by the Continental Army, showed\n       <a href="/wiki/War-weariness" title="War-weariness">\n        war-weariness\n       </a>\n       in what became West Virginia.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trans-Allegheny_Virginia">\n        Trans-Allegheny Virginia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Trans-Allegheny Virginia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/History_of_slavery_in_West_Virginia" title="History of slavery in West Virginia">\n        History of slavery in West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       For more details on this topic, see\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       .\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KitchenBall.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="927" data-file-width="1152" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/KitchenBall.jpg/220px-KitchenBall.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/KitchenBall.jpg/330px-KitchenBall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/KitchenBall.jpg/440px-KitchenBall.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KitchenBall.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A celebration at a slave wedding in Virginia, 1838\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Social conditions in western Virginia were entirely unlike those in the eastern portion of the state. The population was not homogeneous, as a considerable part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">\n        immigration\n       </a>\n       came by way of Pennsylvania and included Germans, Protestant\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scotch-Irish_American" title="Scotch-Irish American">\n        Scotch-Irish\n       </a>\n       , and settlers from the states farther north. Counties in the east and south were settled mostly by east Virginians. During the American Revolution, the movement to create a state beyond the\n       <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Mountains" title="Allegheny Mountains">\n        Alleghenies\n       </a>\n       was revived and a petition for the establishment of "\n       <a href="/wiki/Westsylvania" title="Westsylvania">\n        Westsylvania\n       </a>\n       " was presented to\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">\n        Congress\n       </a>\n       , on the grounds that the mountains presented an almost impassable barrier to the east. The rugged nature of the country made slavery unprofitable, and time only increased the social, political, economic, and cultural differences (\n       <i>\n        see\n       </i>\n       <a href="/wiki/Tuckahoe-Cohee" title="Tuckahoe-Cohee">\n        Tuckahoe-Cohee\n       </a>\n       ) between the two sections of Virginia.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A convention that met in 1829 to form a new constitution for Virginia, against the protest of the counties beyond the mountains, required a property qualification for\n       <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">\n        suffrage\n       </a>\n       . This effectively disenfranchised some of the poorer yeoman farmers. In addition, it gave the slave-holding counties the benefit of three-fifths of their slave population in apportioning the state\'s representation in the U.S. House of Representatives. As a result, every county beyond the Alleghenies except one voted to reject the constitution, which nevertheless passed because of eastern support. The eastern planter elite dominated the legislature and saw to their own interests.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Constitutional_Convention_of_1850" title="Virginia Constitutional Convention of 1850">\n        Virginia Constitutional Convention of 1850\xe2\x80\x9351\n       </a>\n       , the Reform Convention, addressed a number of issues important to western Virginians. It extended the vote to all White males 21 years or older. The governor, lieutenant-governor, the judiciary, sheriffs, and other county officers were to be elected by public vote. The composition of the General Assembly was changed. Representation in the house of delegates was apportioned on the basis of the census of 1850, counting Whites only. The Senate representation was arbitrarily fixed at 50 seats, with the west receiving twenty, and the east thirty senators. This was made acceptable to the west by a provision that required the General Assembly to reapportion representation on the basis of White population in 1865, or else put the matter to a public referendum. But the east also gave itself a tax advantage in requiring a property tax at true and actual value, except for slaves. Slaves under the age of 12 years were not taxed and slaves over that age were taxed at only $300, a fraction of their true value. Small farmers, however, had all their assets, animals, and land taxed at full value. Despite this tax and the lack of\n       <a href="/wiki/Internal_improvements" title="Internal improvements">\n        internal improvements\n       </a>\n       in the west, the vote was 75,748 for and 11,063 against the new Constitution. Most of the opposition came from delegates from eastern counties, who did not like the compromises made for the west.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Given these differences, many in the west had long contemplated a separate state. In particular, men such as lawyer\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis_H._Pierpont" title="Francis H. Pierpont">\n        Francis H. Pierpont\n       </a>\n       from Fairmont, had long chafed under the political domination of the Tidewater and Piedmont slave-holders. In addition to differences over the abolition of slavery, he and allies felt the Virginia government ignored and refused to spend funds on needed internal improvements in the west, such as turnpikes and railroads.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Separation_from_Virginia">\n        Separation from Virginia\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Separation from Virginia">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/State_of_Kanawha" title="State of Kanawha">\n        State of Kanawha\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="West Virginia in the American Civil War">\n        West Virginia in the American Civil War\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francis_Pierpont_portrait.gif">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="288" data-file-width="228" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Francis_Pierpont_portrait.gif/170px-Francis_Pierpont_portrait.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/75/Francis_Pierpont_portrait.gif 1.5x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francis_Pierpont_portrait.gif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis_H._Pierpont" title="Francis H. Pierpont">\n          Francis H. Pierpont\n         </a>\n         , a leader during the Second\n         <a href="/wiki/Wheeling_Convention" title="Wheeling Convention">\n          Wheeling Convention\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg/250px-Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg/375px-Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg/500px-Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Proposed_state_of_kanawha.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         On October 24, 1861, when voters from 41 counties voted to form a new state, voter turnout was 34%. The name was subsequently changed from Kanawha to West Virginia.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n          <a href="#cite_note-21">\n           [21]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg/220px-Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg/330px-Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg/440px-Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abraham_Lincoln_-_WV_Statue.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Abraham Lincoln Walks at Midnight\n         </i>\n         , a statue on the grounds of the West Virginia State Capitol\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="901" data-file-width="1477" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg/220px-Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg/330px-Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg/440px-Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Harper%27s_Ferry_seen_from_Maryland_side_of_Potomac_River.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harpers_Ferry" title="Harpers Ferry">\n          Harpers Ferry\n         </a>\n         (as it appeared in 2005) changed hands a dozen times during the\n         <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">\n          American Civil War\n         </a>\n         and was annexed by West Virginia\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:October_24,_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5100" data-file-width="6587" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/October_24%2C_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg/220px-October_24%2C_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/October_24%2C_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg/330px-October_24%2C_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/October_24%2C_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg/440px-October_24%2C_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:October_24,_1861_county_vote_for_West_Virginia_statehood.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Statehood vote of October 24, 1861\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia was the only state in the Union to separate from a Confederate state (\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       ) during the American Civil War.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In Richmond on April 17, 1861, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Secession_Convention_of_1861" title="Virginia Secession Convention of 1861">\n        Virginia Secession Convention of 1861\n       </a>\n       voted to secede from the Union, but of the 49 delegates from the northwestern corner (which ultimately became West Virginia), only voted 17 in favor of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ordinance_of_Secession" title="Ordinance of Secession">\n        Ordinance of Secession\n       </a>\n       , and 30 voted against,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with 2 abstentions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Almost immediately after that vote, a mass meeting at\n       <a href="/wiki/Clarksburg,_West_Virginia" title="Clarksburg, West Virginia">\n        Clarksburg\n       </a>\n       recommended that each county in northwestern Virginia send delegates to a convention to meet in\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheeling,_West_Virginia" title="Wheeling, West Virginia">\n        Wheeling\n       </a>\n       on May 13, 1861. When this First\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheeling_Convention" title="Wheeling Convention">\n        Wheeling Convention\n       </a>\n       met, 425 delegates from 25 counties were present, though more than one-third of the delegates were from the northern panhandle area,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but soon there was a division of sentiment.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some delegates led by\n       <a href="/wiki/John_S._Carlile" title="John S. Carlile">\n        John S. Carlile\n       </a>\n       favored the immediate formation of a new state, while others led by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waitman_Willey" title="Waitman Willey">\n        Waitman Willey\n       </a>\n       argued that, as Virginia\'s secession had not yet been passed by the required referendum (as happened on May 23), such action would constitute revolution against the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n        <a href="#cite_note-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The convention decided that if Virginians adopted the secession ordinance (of which there was little doubt), another convention including the members-elect of the legislature would meet in Wheeling in June 1861. On May 23, 1861, secession was ratified by a large majority in Virginia as a whole, but in the western counties 34,677 voted against and 19,121 voted for the Ordinance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n        <a href="#cite_note-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Second Wheeling Convention met as agreed on June 11 and declared that, since the Secession Convention had been called without popular consent, all its acts were void and that all who adhered to it had vacated their offices. The Wheeling Conventions, and the delegates themselves, were never actually elected by public ballot to act on behalf of western Virginia.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Of its 103 members, 33 had been elected to the Virginia General Assembly\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       on May 23. This included some hold-over state senators whose four-year terms had begun in 1859, and some who vacated their offices to convene in Wheeling. Other members "were chosen even more irregularly\xe2\x80\x94some in mass meetings, others by county committee, and still others were seemingly self-appointed"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An act for the reorganization of the government was passed on June 19. The next day convention delegates chose\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis_H._Pierpont" title="Francis H. Pierpont">\n        Francis H. Pierpont\n       </a>\n       as governor of Virginia, and elected other officers to a rival state government and two U.S. senators (Willey and Carlile) to replace secessionists before adjourning. The federal government in Washington, D.C. promptly recognized the new government and seated the two new senators. Thus, there were two state governments in Virginia: one pledging allegiance to the United States and one to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">\n        Confederacy\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The second Wheeling Convention had recessed until August 6, then reassembled on August 20 and called for a popular vote on the formation of a new state and for a convention to frame a constitution if the vote should be favorable. At the October 24, 1861 election, 18,408 votes were cast for the new state and only 781 against. The election results were questioned, since the Union army then occupied the area and Union troops were stationed at many of the polls to prevent Confederate sympathizers from voting.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was also election day for local offices, and elections were also held in camps of Confederate soldiers, who elected rival state officials, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Cowan" title="Robert E. Cowan">\n        Robert E. Cowan\n       </a>\n       . Most pro-statehood votes came from 16 counties around the Northern panhandle.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Over 50,000 votes had been cast on the Ordinance of Secession, yet the vote on statehood garnered little more than 19,000.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In Ohio County, home to Wheeling, only about one-quarter of the registered voters cast votes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In most of what would become West Virginia, there was no vote at all, since as two-thirds of the territory of West Virginia had voted for secession and county officers remained loyal to Richmond. Votes recorded from pro-secession counties were mostly cast elsewhere by Unionist refugees from these counties.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Despite that controversy, delegates (including many Methodist ministers) met to write a new Constitution for the new state, beginning on November 26, 1861. During that constitutional convention, a Mr. Lamb of Ohio County and a Mr. Carskadon claimed that in Hampshire County, out of 195 votes only 39 were cast by citizens of the state; the rest were cast illegally by Union soldiers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One of the key figures was Rev.\n       <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Battelle_(minister)" title="Gordon Battelle (minister)">\n        Gordon Battelle\n       </a>\n       , who also represented Ohio County, and who proposed resolutions to establish public schools, as well as to limit movement of slaves into the new state, and to gradually abolish slavery. The education proposal succeeded, but the convention tabled the slavery proposals before finishing its work on February 18, 1862. The new constitution was more closely modeled on that of Ohio than of Virginia, adopting a township model of government rather than the "courthouse cliques" of Virginia which Carlile criticized, and a compromise demanded by the Kanawha region (Charleston lawyers Benjamin Smith and Brown) allowed counties and municipalities to vote subsidies for railroads or other improvement organizations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The resulting instrument was ratified (18,162 for and 514 against) on April 11, 1862.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On May 13, 1862 the state legislature of the reorganized government approved the formation of the new state. An application for admission to the Union was made to Congress, introduced by Senator\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Waitman_Willey" title="Waitman Willey">\n        Waitman Willey\n       </a>\n       of the Restored Government of Virginia. However, Sen. Carlile sought to sabotage the bill, first trying to expand the new state\'s boundaries to include the Shenandoah Valley, and then to defeat the Willey amendment at home.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On December 31, 1862, an enabling act was approved by President\n       <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">\n        Abraham Lincoln\n       </a>\n       admitting West Virginia, on the condition that a provision for the gradual abolition of slavery be inserted in its constitution (as Rev. Battelle had urged in the\n       <i>\n        Wheeling Intelligencer\n       </i>\n       and also written to Lincoln). While many felt that West Virginia\'s admission as a state was both illegal and unconstitutional, Lincoln issued his\n       <i>\n        Opinion on the Admission of West Virginia\n       </i>\n       finding that "the body which consents to the admission of West Virginia is the Legislature of Virginia", and that its admission was therefore both constitutional and expedient.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">\n        <a href="#cite_note-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The convention was reconvened on February 12, 1863, and the abolition demand of the federal enabling act was met. The revised constitution was adopted on March 26, 1863 and on April 20, 1863, President Lincoln issued a proclamation admitting the state 60 days later on June 20, 1863. Meanwhile, officers for the new state were chosen, while Gov. Pierpont moved his pro-Union Virginia capital to Union-occupied\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandria,_Virginia" title="Alexandria, Virginia">\n        Alexandria\n       </a>\n       , where he asserted and exercised jurisdiction over all of the remaining Virginia counties within the federal lines.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The question of the constitutionality of the formation of the new state was later brought before the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">\n        Supreme Court of the United States\n       </a>\n       in the following manner:\n       <a href="/wiki/Berkeley_County,_West_Virginia" title="Berkeley County, West Virginia">\n        Berkeley\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_West_Virginia" title="Jefferson County, West Virginia">\n        Jefferson\n       </a>\n       counties lying on the Potomac east of the mountains, in 1863, with the consent of the reorganized government of Virginia voted in favor of annexation to West Virginia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Many voters of the strongly pro-secessionist counties were absent in the Confederate Army when the vote was taken and refused to acknowledge the transfer when they returned. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_General_Assembly" title="Virginia General Assembly">\n        Virginia General Assembly\n       </a>\n       repealed the act of secession and, in 1866, brought suit against West Virginia asking the court to declare the counties a part of Virginia, which would have declared West Virginia\'s admission as a state unconstitutional. Meanwhile, on March 10, 1866, Congress passed a joint resolution recognizing the transfer. The Supreme Court decided in favor of West Virginia in 1870.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During the Civil War, Union General\n       <a href="/wiki/George_B._McClellan" title="George B. McClellan">\n        George B. McClellan\n       </a>\n       \'s forces gained possession of the greater part of the territory in the summer of 1861, culminating at the\n       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Rich_Mountain" title="Battle of Rich Mountain">\n        Battle of Rich Mountain\n       </a>\n       , and Union control was never again seriously threatened, despite an attempt by\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_E._Lee" title="Robert E. Lee">\n        Robert E. Lee\n       </a>\n       in the same year. In 1863, General\n       <a href="/wiki/John_D._Imboden" title="John D. Imboden">\n        John D. Imboden\n       </a>\n       , with 5,000 Confederates, raided a considerable portion of the state and burned Pierpont\'s library, although Senator Willey escaped their grasp. Bands of guerrillas burned and plundered in some sections, and were not entirely suppressed until after the war ended. The Eastern Panhandle counties were more affected by the war, with military control of the area repeatedly changing hands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The area that became West Virginia actually furnished about an equal number of soldiers to the federal and Confederate armies,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       approximately 22,000\xe2\x80\x9325,000 each. In 1865, the Wheeling government found it necessary to strip voting rights from returning Confederates in order to retain control. James Ferguson, who proposed the law, said that if it was not enacted he would lose election by 500 votes.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">\n        <a href="#cite_note-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The property of Confederates might also be confiscated, and in 1866 a constitutional amendment disfranchising all who had given aid and comfort to the Confederacy was adopted. The addition of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Fourteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">\n        Fourteenth\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Fifteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Fifteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">\n        Fifteenth Amendments\n       </a>\n       to the United States Constitution caused a reaction. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n        Democratic party\n       </a>\n       secured control in 1870, and in 1871, the constitutional amendment of 1866 was abrogated. The first steps toward this change had been taken, however, by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">\n        Republicans\n       </a>\n       in 1870. On August 22, 1872, an entirely new constitution was adopted.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Beginning in\n       <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era" title="Reconstruction Era">\n        Reconstruction\n       </a>\n       , and for several decades thereafter, the two states disputed the new state\'s share of the pre-war Virginia government\'s debts, which had mostly been incurred to finance public infrastructure improvements, such as canals, roads, and railroads under the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Board_of_Public_Works" title="Virginia Board of Public Works">\n        Virginia Board of Public Works\n       </a>\n       . Virginians\xe2\x80\x94led by former Confederate General\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Mahone" title="William Mahone">\n        William Mahone\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94formed a political coalition based upon this: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Readjuster_Party" title="Readjuster Party">\n        Readjuster Party\n       </a>\n       . Although West Virginia\'s first constitution provided for the assumption of a part of the Virginia debt, negotiations opened by Virginia in 1870 were fruitless, and in 1871, Virginia funded two-thirds of the debt and arbitrarily assigned the remainder to West Virginia. The issue was finally settled in 1915, when the\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">\n        Supreme Court of the United States\n       </a>\n       ruled that West Virginia owed Virginia $12,393,929.50.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The final installment of this sum was paid in 1939.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Development_of_natural_resources">\n        Development of natural resources\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Development of natural resources">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">\n   <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trapper_Boy.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="741"    </div>\n         Child labor in the coal mines, West Virginia, 1908 (Photo by\n         <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Hine" title="Lewis Hine">\n          Lewis Hine\n         </a>\n         )\n
