href="/wiki/File:Farm_Security_Administration,_Family_of_coal_miner_in_West_Virginia_-_NARA_-_195846.tif" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Family of coal miner in West Virginia c. 1935\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch,_McDowell_County,_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2476" data-file-width="3000" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch%2C_McDowell_County%2C_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg/220px-Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch%2C_McDowell_County%2C_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch%2C_McDowell_County%2C_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg/330px-Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch%2C_McDowell_County%2C_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch%2C_McDowell_County%2C_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg/440px-Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch%2C_McDowell_County%2C_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saturday_afternoon_street_scene._Welch,_McDowell_County,_West_Virginia._-_NARA_-_541004.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Saturday afternoon street scene,\n         <a href="/wiki/Welch,_West_Virginia" title="Welch, West Virginia">\n          Welch\n         </a>\n         , McDowell County, 1946\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       After\n       <a href="/wiki/Reconstruction_Era" title="Reconstruction Era">\n        Reconstruction\n       </a>\n       , the new 35th state benefited from the development of its mineral resources more than any other single economic activity.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Potassium_nitrate" title="Potassium nitrate">\n        Saltpeter\n       </a>\n       caves had been employed throughout Appalachia for munitions; the border between West Virginia and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       includes the "Saltpeter Trail", a string of\n       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">\n        limestone\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Cave" title="Cave">\n        caverns\n       </a>\n       containing rich deposits of\n       <a href="/wiki/Calcium_nitrate" title="Calcium nitrate">\n        calcium nitrate\n       </a>\n       that were rendered and sold to the government. The trail stretched from\n       <a href="/wiki/Pendleton_County,_West_Virginia" title="Pendleton County, West Virginia">\n        Pendleton County\n       </a>\n       to the western terminus of the route in the town of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Union,_Monroe_County,_West_Virginia" title="Union, Monroe County, West Virginia">\n        Union\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Monroe_County,_West_Virginia" title="Monroe County, West Virginia">\n        Monroe County\n       </a>\n       . Nearly half of these caves are on the West Virginia side, including\n       <a href="/wiki/Organ_Cave" title="Organ Cave">\n        Organ Cave\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Haynes_Cave" title="Haynes Cave">\n        Haynes Cave\n       </a>\n       . In the late 18th-century, saltpeter miners in\n       <a href="/wiki/Haynes_Cave" title="Haynes Cave">\n        Haynes Cave\n       </a>\n       found large animal bones in the deposits. These were sent by a local historian and frontier soldier Colonel John Stuart to\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson" title="Thomas Jefferson">\n        Thomas Jefferson\n       </a>\n       . The bones were named\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megalonyx_jeffersonii" title="Megalonyx jeffersonii">\n         Megalonyx jeffersonii\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , or great-claw, and became known as Jefferson\'s three-toed sloth. It was declared the official\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_fossil" title="State fossil">\n        state fossil\n       </a>\n       of West Virginia in 2008. The West Virginia official\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_minerals,_rocks,_stones_and_gemstones" title="List of U.S. state minerals, rocks, stones and gemstones">\n        state rock\n       </a>\n       is\n       <a href="/wiki/Bituminous_coal" title="Bituminous coal">\n        bituminous coal\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the official\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_minerals,_rocks,_stones_and_gemstones" title="List of U.S. state minerals, rocks, stones and gemstones">\n        state gemstone\n       </a>\n       is silicified Mississippian fossil Lithostrotionella coral.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The limestone also produced a useful\n       <a href="/wiki/Quarry" title="Quarry">\n        quarry\n       </a>\n       industry, usually small, and softer, high-calcium seams were burned to produce industrial lime. This lime was used for agricultural and construction purposes; for many years a specific portion of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C_%26_O_Railroad" title="C &amp; O Railroad">\n        C &amp; O Railroad\n       </a>\n       carried limestone rock to\n       <a href="/wiki/Clifton_Forge,_Virginia" title="Clifton Forge, Virginia">\n        Clifton Forge, Virginia\n       </a>\n       as an industrial flux.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">\n        Salt\n       </a>\n       mining had been underway since the 18th century, though it had largely played out by the time of the American Civil War, when the red salt of\n       <a href="/wiki/Kanawha_County,_West_Virginia" title="Kanawha County, West Virginia">\n        Kanawha County\n       </a>\n       was a valued commodity of first Confederate, and later Union, forces. In years following, more sophisticated mining methods would restore West Virginia\'s role as a major producer of salt.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       However, in the second half of the 19th century, there was an even greater treasure not yet developed:\n       <a href="/wiki/Bituminous_coal" title="Bituminous coal">\n        bituminous coal\n       </a>\n       . It would fuel much of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">\n        Industrial Revolution\n       </a>\n       in the U.S. and the steamships of many of the world\'s navies.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The residents (both Native Americans and early European settlers) had long known of the underlying coal, and that it could be used for heating and fuel. However, for a long time, very small "personal" mines were the only practical development. After the War, with the new\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railroad" title="Railroad">\n        railroads\n       </a>\n       came a practical method to transport large quantities of coal to expanding U.S. and export markets. As the\n       <a href="/wiki/Anthracite" title="Anthracite">\n        anthracite\n       </a>\n       mines of northwestern New Jersey and Pennsylvania began to play out during this same time period, investors and industrialists focused new interest in West Virginia.\n       <a href="/wiki/Geologist" title="Geologist">\n        Geologists\n       </a>\n       such as Dr.\n       <a href="/wiki/David_T._Ansted" title="David T. Ansted">\n        David T. Ansted\n       </a>\n       surveyed potential coal fields and invested in land and early mining projects.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The completion of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Ohio_Railway" title="Chesapeake and Ohio Railway">\n        Chesapeake and Ohio Railway\n       </a>\n       (C&amp;O) across the state to the new city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_West_Virginia" title="Huntington, West Virginia">\n        Huntington\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">\n        Ohio River\n       </a>\n       in 1872 opened access to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_River_(West_Virginia)" title="New River (West Virginia)">\n        New River\n       </a>\n       Coal Field. Soon, the C&amp;O was building its huge\n       <a href="/wiki/Coal_pier" title="Coal pier">\n        coal pier\n       </a>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Newport_News,_Virginia" title="Newport News, Virginia">\n        Newport News, Virginia\n       </a>\n       on the large harbor of\n       <a href="/wiki/Hampton_Roads" title="Hampton Roads">\n        Hampton Roads\n       </a>\n       . In 1881, the new Philadelphia-based owners of the former\n       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic,_Mississippi_and_Ohio_Railroad" title="Atlantic, Mississippi and Ohio Railroad">\n        Atlantic, Mississippi and Ohio Railroad\n       </a>\n       (AM&amp;O), which stretched across Virginia\'s southern tier from\n       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk,_Virginia" title="Norfolk, Virginia">\n        Norfolk\n       </a>\n       , had sights clearly set on the Mountain State, where the owners had large land holdings. Their railroad was renamed\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_and_Western" title="Norfolk and Western">\n        Norfolk and Western\n       </a>\n       (N&amp;W), and a new railroad city was developed at\n       <a href="/wiki/Roanoke,_Virginia" title="Roanoke, Virginia">\n        Roanoke\n       </a>\n       to handle planned expansion. After its new president\n       <a href="/wiki/Frederick_J._Kimball" title="Frederick J. Kimball">\n        Frederick J. Kimball\n       </a>\n       and a small party journeyed by horseback and saw firsthand the rich bituminous coal seam, which Kimball\'s wife named\n       <i>\n        Pocahontas\n       </i>\n       , the N&amp;W redirected its planned westward expansion to reach it. Soon, the N&amp;W was also shipping from new coal piers at Hampton Roads.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1889, in the southern part of the state, along the Norfolk and Western rail lines, the important coal center of\n       <a href="/wiki/Bluefield,_West_Virginia" title="Bluefield, West Virginia">\n        Bluefield, West Virginia\n       </a>\n       was founded. The "capital" of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pocahontas_coalfield" title="Pocahontas coalfield">\n        Pocahontas coalfield\n       </a>\n       , this city would remain the largest city in the southern portion of the state for several decades. It shares a sister city with the same name, Bluefield, in Virginia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the northern portion of the state and elsewhere, the older\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore_and_Ohio_Railroad" title="Baltimore and Ohio Railroad">\n        Baltimore and Ohio Railroad\n       </a>\n       (B&amp;O) and other lines also expanded to take advantage of coal opportunities. The B&amp;O developed coal piers in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baltimore,_Maryland" title="Baltimore, Maryland">\n        Baltimore\n       </a>\n       and at several points on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       . Other significant rail carriers of coal were the\n       <a href="/wiki/Western_Maryland_Railway" title="Western Maryland Railway">\n        Western Maryland Railway\n       </a>\n       (WM),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southern_Railway_(US)" title="Southern Railway (US)">\n        Southern Railway\n       </a>\n       (SOU), and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Louisville_and_Nashville_Railroad" title="Louisville and Nashville Railroad">\n        Louisville and Nashville Railroad\n       </a>\n       (L&amp;N).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Particularly notable was a latecomer, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginian_Railway" title="Virginian Railway">\n        Virginian Railway\n       </a>\n       (VGN). By 1900, only a large area of the most rugged terrain of southern West Virginia was any distance from the existing railroads and mining activity. Within this area west of the New River Coalfield in Raleigh and Wyoming counties lay the\n       <a href="/wiki/Winding_Gulf_Coalfield" title="Winding Gulf Coalfield">\n        Winding Gulf Coalfield\n       </a>\n       , later promoted as the "Billion Dollar Coalfield."\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A prot\xc3\xa9g\xc3\xa9 of Dr. Ansted was\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/William_N._Page" title="William N. Page">\n        William Nelson Page\n       </a>\n       (1854\xe2\x80\x931932), a\n       <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineer" title="Civil engineer">\n        civil engineer\n       </a>\n       and mining manager in\n       <a href="/wiki/Fayette_County,_West_Virginia" title="Fayette County, West Virginia">\n        Fayette County\n       </a>\n       . Former West Virginia Governor\n       <a href="/wiki/William_A._MacCorkle" title="William A. MacCorkle">\n        William A. MacCorkle\n       </a>\n       described him as a man who knew the land "as a farmer knows a field." Beginning in 1898, Page teamed with northern and European-based investors to take advantage of the undeveloped area. They acquired large tracts of land in the area, and Page began the\n       <a href="/wiki/Deepwater_Railway" title="Deepwater Railway">\n        Deepwater Railway\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short-line_railroad" title="Short-line railroad">\n        short-line railroad\n       </a>\n       chartered to stretch between the C&amp;O at its line along the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kanawha_River" title="Kanawha River">\n        Kanawha River\n       </a>\n       and the N&amp;W at\n       <a href="/wiki/Matoaka,_West_Virginia" title="Matoaka, West Virginia">\n        Matoaka\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94a distance of about 80 miles (130\xc2\xa0km).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Although the Deepwater plan should have provided a competitive shipping market via either railroad, leaders of the two large railroads did not appreciate the scheme. In secret collusion, each declined to negotiate favorable rates with Page, nor did they offer to purchase his railroad, as they had many other short-lines. However, if the C&amp;O and N&amp;W presidents thought they could thus kill the Page project, they were to be proved mistaken. One of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Partnership" title="Partnership">\n        silent partner\n       </a>\n       investors Page had enlisted was millionaire industrialist\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Henry_H._Rogers" title="Henry H. Rogers">\n        Henry Huttleston Rogers\n       </a>\n       , a principal in\n       <a href="/wiki/John_D._Rockefeller" title="John D. Rockefeller">\n        John D. Rockefeller\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_Oil_Trust" title="Standard Oil Trust">\n        Standard Oil Trust\n       </a>\n       and an old hand at developing natural resources and transportation. A master at competitive "warfare", Henry Rogers did not like to lose in his endeavors and also had\n       <a href="/wiki/Deep_pocket" title="Deep pocket">\n        "deep pockets"\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Instead of giving up, Page (and Rogers) quietly planned and then built their tracks all the way east across Virginia, using Rogers\' private fortune to finance the $40-million cost. When the renamed\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginian_Railway" title="Virginian Railway">\n        Virginian Railway\n       </a>\n       (VGN) was completed in 1909, no fewer than three railroads were shipping ever-increasing volumes of coal to export from Hampton Roads. West Virginia coal was also under high demand at\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes" title="Great Lakes">\n        Great Lakes\n       </a>\n       ports. The VGN and the N&amp;W ultimately became parts of the modern\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" title="Norfolk Southern">\n        Norfolk Southern\n       </a>\n       system, and the VGN\'s well-engineered 21st-century tracks continue to offer a favorable gradient to Hampton Roads.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As coal mining and related work became major employment activities in the state, there was considerable labor strife as working conditions, safety issues and economic concerns arose. Even in the 21st century, mining safety and ecological concerns is still challenging to the state whose coal continues to power electrical generating plants in many other states.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Coal is not the only valuable mineral found in West Virginia, as the state was the site of the 1928 discovery of the 34.48 carat (6.896 g)\n       <a href="/wiki/Jones_Diamond" title="Jones Diamond">\n        Jones Diamond\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">\n        Geography\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geography_of_West_Virginia" title="Geography of West Virginia">\n        Geography of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westvirginia_schild.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="938" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Westvirginia_schild.jpg/220px-Westvirginia_schild.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Westvirginia_schild.jpg/330px-Westvirginia_schild.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Westvirginia_schild.jpg/440px-Westvirginia_schild.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westvirginia_schild.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         State sign (\n         <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_52" title="U.S. Route 52">\n          Highway 52\n         </a>\n         )\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WV_plateau.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="784" data-file-width="800" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/WV_plateau.jpg/220px-WV_plateau.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/WV_plateau.jpg/330px-WV_plateau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/WV_plateau.jpg/440px-WV_plateau.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WV_plateau.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Shaded relief map of the\n         <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Plateau" title="Cumberland Plateau">\n          Cumberland Plateau\n         </a>\n         and\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ridge-and-valley_Appalachians" title="Ridge-and-valley Appalachians">\n          Ridge-and-valley Appalachians\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WVirginiaCo.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1967" data-file-width="2307" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/WVirginiaCo.png/220px-WVirginiaCo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/WVirginiaCo.png/330px-WVirginiaCo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/WVirginiaCo.png/440px-WVirginiaCo.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WVirginiaCo.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Map of\n         <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_West_Virginia" title="List of counties in West Virginia">\n          West Virginia counties\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Located in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">\n        Appalachian Mountain range\n       </a>\n       , West Virginia covers an area of 24,229.76 square miles (62,754.8\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ), with 24,077.73 square miles (62,361.0\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of land and 152.03 square miles (393.8\xc2\xa0km\n       <sup>\n        2\n       </sup>\n       ) of water, making it the 41st-largest state in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia borders Pennsylvania and Maryland in the northeast, Virginia in the southeast, Ohio in the northwest, and Kentucky in the southwest. Its longest border is with Virginia at 381 miles, followed by Ohio at 243 miles, Maryland at 174 miles, Pennsylvania at 118 miles, and Kentucky at 79 miles.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology_and_terrain">\n        Geology and terrain\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geology and terrain">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_West_Virginia" title="Geology of West Virginia">\n        Geology of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spruce_Knob.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Spruce_Knob.jpg/220px-Spruce_Knob.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Spruce_Knob.jpg/330px-Spruce_Knob.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Spruce_Knob.jpg/440px-Spruce_Knob.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spruce_Knob.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The summit of\n         <a href="/wiki/Spruce_Knob" title="Spruce Knob">\n          Spruce Knob\n         </a>\n         is often covered in clouds\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia is located entirely within the Appalachian Region, and the state is almost entirely mountainous, giving reason to the nickname\n       <i>\n        The Mountain State\n       </i>\n       and the motto\n       <i>\n        Montani Semper Liberi\n       </i>\n       ("Mountaineers are always free"). The elevations and ruggedness drop near large rivers like the Ohio River or\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_River" title="Shenandoah River">\n        Shenandoah River\n       </a>\n       . About 75% of the state is within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Plateau" title="Cumberland Plateau">\n        Cumberland Plateau\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_Plateau" title="Allegheny Plateau">\n        Allegheny Plateau\n       </a>\n       regions. Though the relief is not high, the plateau region is extremely rugged in most areas. The average elevation of West Virginia is approximately 1,500 feet (460\xc2\xa0m) above sea level, which is the highest of any U.S. state east of the Mississippi River.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On the eastern state line with\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       , high peaks in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_National_Forest" title="Monongahela National Forest">\n        Monongahela National Forest\n       </a>\n       region give rise to an island of colder\n       <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">\n        climate\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">\n        ecosystems\n       </a>\n       similar to those of northern\n       <a href="/wiki/New_England" title="New England">\n        New England\n       </a>\n       and eastern Canada. The highest point in the state is atop\n       <a href="/wiki/Spruce_Knob" title="Spruce Knob">\n        Spruce Knob\n       </a>\n       , at 4,863 feet (1,482\xc2\xa0m),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usgs_48-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-usgs-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and is covered in a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boreal_forest" title="Boreal forest">\n        boreal forest\n       </a>\n       of dense\n       <a href="/wiki/Spruce" title="Spruce">\n        spruce\n       </a>\n       trees at altitudes above 4,000 feet (1,200\xc2\xa0m). Spruce Knob lies within the Monongahela National Forest and is a part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Spruce_Knob-Seneca_Rocks_National_Recreation_Area" title="Spruce Knob-Seneca Rocks National Recreation Area">\n        Spruce Knob-Seneca Rocks National Recreation Area\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A total of six\n       <a href="/wiki/Wilderness" title="Wilderness">\n        wilderness\n       </a>\n       areas can also be found within the forest. Outside the forest to the south, the New River Gorge is a canyon 1,000 feet (300\xc2\xa0m) deep, carved by the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_River_(Kanawha_River)" title="New River (Kanawha River)">\n        New River\n       </a>\n       . The\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">\n        National Park Service\n       </a>\n       manages a portion of the gorge and river that has been designated as the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_River_Gorge_National_River" title="New River Gorge National River">\n        New River Gorge National River\n       </a>\n       , one of only 15 rivers in the U.S. with this level of protection.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other areas under protection and management include:\n      </p>\n      <table border="0">\n       <tr>\n        <td valign="top">\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appalachian_National_Scenic_Trail" title="Appalachian National Scenic Trail">\n            Appalachian National Scenic Trail\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Bluestone_National_Scenic_River" title="Bluestone National Scenic River">\n            Bluestone National Scenic River\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Canaan_Valley_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Canaan Valley National Wildlife Refuge">\n            Canaan Valley National Wildlife Refuge\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Chesapeake_and_Ohio_Canal_National_Historical_Park" title="Chesapeake and Ohio Canal National Historical Park">\n            Chesapeake and Ohio Canal National Historical Park\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </td>\n        <td valign="top">\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Gauley_River_National_Recreation_Area" title="Gauley River National Recreation Area">\n            Gauley River National Recreation Area\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/George_Washington_National_Forest" title="George Washington National Forest">\n            George Washington National Forest\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Harpers_Ferry_National_Historical_Park" title="Harpers Ferry National Historical Park">\n            Harpers Ferry National Historical Park\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River_Islands_National_Wildlife_Refuge" title="Ohio River Islands National Wildlife Refuge">\n            Ohio River Islands National Wildlife Refuge\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Most of West Virginia lies within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_mixed_mesophytic_forests" title="Appalachian mixed mesophytic forests">\n        Appalachian mixed mesophytic forests\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">\n        ecoregion\n       </a>\n       , while the higher elevations along the eastern border and in the panhandle lie within the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian-Blue_Ridge_forests" title="Appalachian-Blue Ridge forests">\n        Appalachian-Blue Ridge forests\n       </a>\n       . The native\n       <a href="/wiki/Vegetation" title="Vegetation">\n        vegetation\n       </a>\n       for most of the state was originally mixed\n       <a href="/wiki/Hardwood" title="Hardwood">\n        hardwood\n       </a>\n       forest of oak,\n       <a href="/wiki/Chestnut" title="Chestnut">\n        chestnut\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Maple" title="Maple">\n        maple\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Beech" title="Beech">\n        beech\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_white_pine" title="Eastern white pine">\n        white pine\n       </a>\n       , with\n       <a href="/wiki/Willow" title="Willow">\n        willow\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_sycamore" title="American sycamore">\n        American sycamore\n       </a>\n       along the state\'s waterways. Many of the areas are rich in\n       <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">\n        biodiversity\n       </a>\n       and scenic beauty, a fact that is appreciated by native West Virginians, who refer to their home as\n       <i>\n        Almost Heaven\n       </i>\n       (from the song, "\n       <a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Home,_Country_Roads" title="Take Me Home, Country Roads">\n        Take Me Home, Country Roads\n       </a>\n       " by\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Denver" title="John Denver">\n        John Denver\n       </a>\n       ). Before the song, it was known as "The Cog State" (Coal, Oil, and Gas) or "The Mountain State".\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The underlying rock strata are\n       <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">\n        sandstone\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">\n        shale\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Bituminous_coal" title="Bituminous coal">\n        bituminous coal\n       </a>\n       beds, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">\n        limestone\n       </a>\n       laid down in a near-shore environment from\n       <a href="/wiki/Sediment" title="Sediment">\n        sediments\n       </a>\n       derived from mountains to the east, in a shallow inland sea on the west. Some beds illustrate a coastal swamp environment, some river delta, some shallow water. Sea level rose and fell many times during the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mississippian_age" title="Mississippian age">\n        Mississippian\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvanian_(geology)" title="Pennsylvanian (geology)">\n        Pennsylvanian\n       </a>\n       eras, giving a variety of rock\n       <a href="/wiki/Stratum" title="Stratum">\n        strata\n       </a>\n       . The Appalachian Mountains are some of the oldest on earth, having formed over 300\xc2\xa0million years ago.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">\n        Climate\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Climate">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n      </div>\n             <div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:6.8288888888889em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right">\n              <span style="font-size:80%">\n         <div style="height:0em;bottom:2em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #abc;padding:0;margin:0">\n             </div>\n             <div </div>\n             <div style="height:0em;bottom:8em;width:1.6em;position:absolute;left:0;border-bottom:dotted 1px #cba;padding:0;margin:0">\n             </div>\n             <div </span>\n             </div>\n             <div style="color:red;position:absolute;bottom:5.94em; left:-.4em;width:1.6em;height:1.5em;text-align:right">\n              <span style="font-size:80%">\n               \xe2\x88\x923\n              </span>\n             </div>\n            </div>\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td colspan="12" style="padding: 2px;   </table>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg/220px-Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg/330px-Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg/440px-Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Blackwater-canyon-fall-colors_-_West_Virginia_-_ForestWander.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Blackwater_Canyon" title="Blackwater Canyon">\n          Blackwater Canyon\n         </a>\n         during autumn\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The climate of West Virginia is generally a\n       <a href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate" title="Humid subtropical climate">\n        humid subtropical climate\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">\n        K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        Cfa\n       </i>\n       , except\n       <i>\n        Dfb\n       </i>\n       at the higher elevations) with warm to hot, humid summers and chilly winters, increasing in severity with elevation. Some southern highland areas also have a mountain temperate climate (K\xc3\xb6ppen\n       <i>\n        Cfb\n       </i>\n       ) where winter temperatures are more moderate and summer temperatures are somewhat cooler. However, the weather is subject in all parts of the state to change. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">\n        hardiness zones\n       </a>\n       range from zone 5b in the central\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">\n        Appalachian\n       </a>\n       mountains to zone 7a in the warmest parts of the lowest elevations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG/220px-Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG/330px-Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG/440px-Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lightning_over_Cacapon_Mountain_in_West_Virginia_Skies_2.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lightning over Cacapon Mountain in West Virginia Skies\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In the Eastern Panhandle and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">\n        Ohio River\n       </a>\n       Valley, temperatures are warm enough to see and grow subtropical plants such as southern magnolia (\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Magnolia_grandiflora" title="Magnolia grandiflora">\n         Magnolia grandiflora\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/Lagerstroemia" title="Lagerstroemia">\n        crepe myrtle\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Albizia_julibrissin" title="Albizia julibrissin">\n         Albizia julibrissin\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_sweetgum" title="American sweetgum">\n        American sweetgum\n       </a>\n       and even the occasional\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Needle_palm" title="Needle palm">\n        needle palm\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Sabal_minor" title="Sabal minor">\n        sabal minor\n       </a>\n       . These plants do not thrive as well in other parts of the state. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_prickly_pear" title="Eastern prickly pear">\n        eastern prickly pear\n       </a>\n       grows well in many portions of the state.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Average January temperatures range from around 26\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x924\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) near the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cheat_River" title="Cheat River">\n        Cheat River\n       </a>\n       to 41\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (5\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) along sections of the border with Kentucky. July averages range from 67\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (19\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) along the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Branch_Potomac_River" title="North Branch Potomac River">\n        North Branch Potomac River\n       </a>\n       to 76\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (24\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) in the western part of the state. It is cooler in the mountains than in the lower sections of the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climates_52-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-climates-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The highest recorded temperature in the state is 112\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (44\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) at\n       <a href="/wiki/Martinsburg,_West_Virginia" title="Martinsburg, West Virginia">\n        Martinsburg\n       </a>\n       on July 10, 1936 and the lowest recorded temperature in the state is \xe2\x88\x9237\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0F (\xe2\x88\x9238\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C) at\n       <a href="/wiki/Lewisburg,_West_Virginia" title="Lewisburg, West Virginia">\n        Lewisburg\n       </a>\n       on December 30, 1917.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG/220px-Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG/330px-Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG/440px-Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dec_18th_and_19th_Significant_Snowstorm_in_West_Virginia_3.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         December 18 and 19, 2003. Significant snowstorm in West Virginia\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Annual precipitation ranges from less than 32 inches (81\xc2\xa0cm) in the lower eastern section to more than 56 inches (140\xc2\xa0cm) in higher parts of the Allegheny Front. Valleys in the east have lower rainfall because the Allegheny mountain ridges to the west create a partial\n       <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">\n        rain shadow\n       </a>\n       . Slightly more than half the rainfall occurs from April to September. Dense fogs are common in many valleys of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Kanawha_County,_West_Virginia" title="Kanawha County, West Virginia">\n        Kanawha\n       </a>\n       section, especially the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tygart_Valley" title="Tygart Valley">\n        Tygart Valley\n       </a>\n       . West Virginia is also one of the cloudiest states in the nation, with the cities of\n       <a href="/wiki/Elkins,_West_Virginia" title="Elkins, West Virginia">\n        Elkins\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Beckley,_West_Virginia" title="Beckley, West Virginia">\n        Beckley\n       </a>\n       ranking 9th and 10th in the U.S. respectively for the number of cloudy days per year (over 210). In addition to persistent cloudy skies caused by the damming of moisture by the Alleghenies, West Virginia also experiences some of the most frequent precipitation in the nation, with\n       <a href="/wiki/Snowshoe,_West_Virginia" title="Snowshoe, West Virginia">\n        Snowshoe\n       </a>\n       averaging nearly 200 days a year with either rain or snow. Snow usually lasts only a few days in the lower sections but may persist for weeks in the higher mountain areas. An average of 34 inches (86\xc2\xa0cm) of snow falls annually in Charleston, although during the winter of 1995\xe2\x80\x931996 more than three times that amount fell as several cities in the state established new records for snowfall. Average snowfall in the Allegheny Highlands can range up to 180 inches (460\xc2\xa0cm) per year. Severe weather is somewhat less prevalent in West Virginia than in most other eastern states, and it ranks among the least tornado-prone states east of the Rockies.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n    </a>\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px;">\n         1,793,477\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size:85%">\n        </td>\n        <td      </td>\n        <td style="font-size:85%">\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">\n         0.8%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center">\n         <b>\n          Est. 2016\n         </b>\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px;">\n         1,831,102\n        </td>\n        <td style="font-size:85%">\n        </td>\n        <td style="padding-left:8px; text-align: center;">\n         \xe2\x88\x921.2%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black; font-size:85%; text-align:center">\n         Source: 1910\xe2\x80\x932010\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n          <a href="#cite_note-53">\n           [53]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <br/>\n         2015 Estimate\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_54-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-54">\n           [54]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">\n        United States Census Bureau\n       </a>\n       estimates that the population of West Virginia was 1,831,102 on July 1, 2016, a 1.2% decrease since the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">\n        2010 United States Census\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_54-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">\n        center of population\n       </a>\n       of West Virginia is located in\n       <a href="/wiki/Braxton_County,_West_Virginia" title="Braxton County, West Virginia">\n        Braxton County\n       </a>\n       , in the town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Gassaway,_West_Virginia" title="Gassaway, West Virginia">\n        Gassaway\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       At the 2010 Census, the racial composition of the state\'s population was:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        93.2% of the population was\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_White" title="Non-Hispanic White">\n         non-Hispanic White\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        3.4% non-Hispanic Black or\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">\n         African American\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        0.2% non-Hispanic\n        <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n         American Indian\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alaska_Native" title="Alaska Native">\n         Alaska Native\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        0.7% non-Hispanic\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">\n         Asian American\n        </a>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        0.1% from some other race (non-Hispanic)\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        1.3%\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">\n         Multiracial American\n        </a>\n        (non-Hispanic).\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       In the same year, 1.2% of West Virginia\'s population was of Hispanic, Latino, or Spanish origin (they may be of any race).\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">\n       <caption>\n        <b>\n         West Virginia Racial Breakdown of Population\n        </b>\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Racial composition\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         1990\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n          <a </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">\n          Black\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n <td>\n         0.7%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">\n          Native\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.1%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.2%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.2%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_Hawaiian" title="Native Hawaiian">\n          Native Hawaiian\n         </a>\n         and\n         <br/>\n         <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islander" title="Pacific Islander">\n          other Pacific Islander\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States_Census"     <td>\n         0.3%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multiracial_American" title="Multiracial American">\n          Two or more races\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         0.9%\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1.5%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       As of 2012, West Virginia has an estimated population of 1,855,413, which is an increase of 49, or 0.0%, from the prior year and an increase of 2,414, or 0.13%, since the year 2000. This includes a natural decrease since the last census of 3,296 people (that is 108,292 births minus 111,588 deaths) and an increase from net\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_migration" title="Human migration">\n        migration\n       </a>\n       of 14,209 people into the state. West Virginia is the least populous\n       <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_United_States" title="Southeastern United States">\n        southeastern state\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Immigration to the United States">\n        Immigration\n       </a>\n       from outside the United States resulted in a net increase of 3,691 people, and migration within the country produced a net increase of 10,518 people.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Only 1.1% of the state\'s residents were foreign-born, placing West Virginia last among the 50 states in that statistic. It also has the lowest percentage of residents that speak a language other than English in the home (2.7%).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The five largest ancestry groups in West Virginia are:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">\n        German\n       </a>\n       (18.9%),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">\n        Irish\n       </a>\n       (15.1%)\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic_American" title="Ethnic American">\n        American\n       </a>\n       (12.9%),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">\n        English\n       </a>\n       (11.8%) and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_American" title="Italian American">\n        Italian\n       </a>\n       (4.7%)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 2000 Census People who identified their ethnicity as simply American made up 18.7% of the population.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The majority of these people are of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots-Irish_American" title="Scots-Irish American">\n        Scots-Irish\n       </a>\n       ancestry, or of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">\n        English\n       </a>\n       descent.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Large numbers of people of\n       <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">\n        German\n       </a>\n       ancestry are present in the northeastern counties of the state. People of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">\n        English\n       </a>\n       ancestry are present throughout the entire state. Many West Virginians who self-identify as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">\n        Irish\n       </a>\n       are actually\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scots-Irish_American" title="Scots-Irish American">\n        Scots-Irish\n       </a>\n       Protestants.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       5.6% of West Virginia\'s population were reported as under 5, 22.3% under 18, and 15.3% were 65 or older. Females made up approximately 51.4% of the population.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There were 20,928 births in 2006. Of these, 19,757 (94.40% of the births, 95.19% of the population) were to Non-Hispanic Whites. There were 22 births to American Indians (0.11% of the births and 0.54% of the population), 177 births to Asians (0.85% of the births and 0.68% of the population), 219 births to Hispanics (1.05% of the births and 0.88% of the population) and 753 births to Blacks and others (3.60% of the births and 3.56% of the population).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The state\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Panhandle_of_West_Virginia" title="Northern Panhandle of West Virginia">\n        Northern Panhandle\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North-Central_West_Virginia" title="North-Central West Virginia">\n        North-Central\n       </a>\n       region feel an affinity for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" title="Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">\n        Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania\n       </a>\n       . Also, those in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Panhandle_of_West_Virginia" title="Eastern Panhandle of West Virginia">\n        Eastern Panhandle\n       </a>\n       feel a connection with the Washington, D.C. suburbs in\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_West_Virginia" title="Southern West Virginia">\n        southern West Virginians\n       </a>\n       often consider themselves\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">\n        Southerners\n       </a>\n       . Finally, the towns and farms along the mid-\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">\n        Ohio River\n       </a>\n       , which forms most of the state\'s western border, have an appearance and culture somewhat resembling the\n       <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">\n        Midwest\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">\n        <a href="#cite_note-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="navbox">\n       <tr>\n        <th class="navbox-title" colspan="10">\n </td>\n        <td>\n         <b>\n          19,805\n         </b>\n         (100%)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">\n        Religion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:15px; margin-top:0;">\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="3" style="background:#ccf;">\n         Religion (ARIS 2008)\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="border-bottom:0;">\n         <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">\n          Christian\n <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">\n          Baptist\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         27%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">\n          Roman Catholic\n         </a>\n       </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         13%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">\n
