  <td align="right">\n         5%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         Unaffiliated\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         15%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="border-bottom:0;">\n         Other Religions\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         3%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:15px; margin-top:0;">\n       <tr>\n        <th colspan="3" style="background:#ccf;">\n         Religion (Pew Forum 2014)\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n          <a href="#cite_note-68">\n           [68]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td rowspan="6" style="border-top:0; border-bottom:0;">\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Christian" title="Evangelical Christian">\n          Evangelical Christian\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         39%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Mainline_Protestant" title="Mainline Protestant">\n          Mainline Protestant\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         29%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">\n          Roman Catholic\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         6%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon" title="Mormon">\n          Mormon\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         2%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">\n          Jewish\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         1%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">\n          Muslim\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         1%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="3" style="border-top:0;">\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         Don\'t Know/Refused\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         1%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         Unaffiliated\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         18%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td colspan="2" style="border-bottom:0;">\n         Other Religions\n        </td>\n        <td align="right">\n         3%\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       Several surveys have been made in recent years, in 2008 by the American Religion Identity Survey,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in 2010 by the Pew Forum on Religion and Public Life.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Pew survey results admit to a 6.5% margin of error plus or minus, while the ARIS survey states that "estimates are subject to larger sampling errors in states with small populations." A characteristic of religion in Appalachian communities is the abundance of independent, non-affiliated churches, which "remain unnoted and uncounted in any census of church life in the United States." This sometimes leads to the belief that these communities are "unchurched".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The largest denomination as of 2010 was the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">\n        United Methodist Church\n       </a>\n       with 136,000 members in 1,200 congregations. The second largest Protestant church was the\n       <a href="/wiki/American_Baptist_Churches_USA" title="American Baptist Churches USA">\n        American Baptist Churches USA\n       </a>\n       with 88,000 members and 381 congregations. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Baptist_Convention" title="Southern Baptist Convention">\n        Southern Baptist\n       </a>\n       church had 44,000 members and 232 congregations. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Churches_of_Christ" title="Churches of Christ">\n        Churches of Christ\n       </a>\n       had 22,000 members and 287 congregations. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_(USA)" title="Presbyterian Church (USA)">\n        Presbyterian Church (USA)\n       </a>\n       had 200 congregations and 20,000 members.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A survey conducted in 2015 by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">\n        Pew Research Center\n       </a>\n       found that West Virginia was the 7th most "highly religious" state in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_West_Virginia" title="Economy of West Virginia">\n        Economy of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Virginia_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="West Virginia locations by per capita income">\n        West Virginia locations by per capita income\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">\n        Overview\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Overview">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The economy of West Virginia nominally would be the 62nd largest economy globally behind\n       <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">\n        Iraq\n       </a>\n       and ahead of\n       <a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">\n        Croatia\n       </a>\n       according to 2009\n       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">\n        World Bank\n       </a>\n       projections,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the 64th largest behind Iraq and ahead of\n       <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">\n        Libya\n       </a>\n       according to 2009\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">\n        International Monetary Fund\n       </a>\n       projections.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state has a projected nominal GSP of $63.34 billion in 2009 according to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">\n        Bureau of Economic Analysis\n       </a>\n       report of November 2010, and a real GSP of $55.04 billion. The real GDP growth of the state in 2009 of .7% was the 7th best in the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BEA_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BEA-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia was only one of ten states in 2009 that grew economically.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While per capita income fell 2.6% nationally in 2009, West Virginia\'s grew at 1.8%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WVC_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WVC-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Through the first half of 2010, exports from West Virginia topped $3 billion, growing 39.5% over the same period from the previous year and ahead of the national average by 15.7%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WVC_78-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WVC-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Morgantown,_West_Virginia" title="Morgantown, West Virginia">\n        Morgantown\n       </a>\n       was ranked by\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">\n         Forbes\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       as the #10 best small city in the nation to conduct business in 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MMF_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MMF-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The city is also home to\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_University" title="West Virginia University">\n        West Virginia University\n       </a>\n       , the 95th best public university according to U.S. News &amp; World Report in 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The proportion of West Virginia\'s adult population with a\n       <a href="/wiki/Bachelor%27s_degree" title="Bachelor\'s degree">\n        bachelor\'s degree\n       </a>\n       is the lowest in the U.S. at 17.3%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">\n        <a href="#cite_note-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The net corporate income tax rate is 6.5% while business costs are 13% below the national average.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The U.S. Bureau of Economic Analysis reported that in 2014 West Virginia\'s economy grew twice as fast as the next fastest growing state East of the Mississippi River, ranking third alongside Wyoming and just behind North Dakota and Texas among the fastest growing states in the United States.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">\n        Tourism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tourism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Tourism contributed $4.27 billion to the state\'s economy and employed 44,400 people in 2010, making it one of the state\'s largest industries.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Many tourists, especially in the eastern mountains, are drawn to the region\'s notable opportunities for outdoor recreation.\n       <a href="/wiki/Canaan_Valley" title="Canaan Valley">\n        Canaan Valley\n       </a>\n       is popular for winter sports,\n       <a href="/wiki/Seneca_Rocks" title="Seneca Rocks">\n        Seneca Rocks\n       </a>\n       is one of the premier rock climbing destinations in the eastern U.S., the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_River_Gorge" title="New River Gorge">\n        New River Gorge\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_WV" title="Fayetteville, WV">\n        Fayetteville\n       </a>\n       area draws rock climbers as well as\n       <a href="/wiki/Whitewater" title="Whitewater">\n        whitewater\n       </a>\n       rafting enthusiasts, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_National_Forest" title="Monongahela National Forest">\n        Monongahela National Forest\n       </a>\n       is popular with hikers, backpackers, hunters, and anglers.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3464" data-file-width="5201" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg/300px-Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg/450px-Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg/600px-Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Seneca_Rocks_by_Asilverstein_Oct_2013_High_Dynamic_Range_Merge_from_7_Exposures.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Seneca Rocks, Pendleton County\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In addition to such outdoor recreation opportunities, the state offers a number of historic and cultural attractions.\n       <a href="/wiki/Harpers_Ferry_National_Historical_Park" title="Harpers Ferry National Historical Park">\n        Harpers Ferry National Historical Park\n       </a>\n       is a historic town situated at the confluence of the Shenandoah and Potomac rivers.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harpers_Ferry" title="Harpers Ferry">\n        Harpers Ferry\n       </a>\n       was the site of\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Brown_(abolitionist)" title="John Brown (abolitionist)">\n        John Brown\n       </a>\n       \'s 1859 slave revolt and\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Brown%27s_raid_on_Harpers_Ferry" title="John Brown\'s raid on Harpers Ferry">\n        raid\n       </a>\n       on the US Armory and Arsenal. Located at the approximate midpoint of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Trail" title="Appalachian Trail">\n        Appalachian Trail\n       </a>\n       , Harpers Ferry is the base of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Trail_Conservancy" title="Appalachian Trail Conservancy">\n        Appalachian Trail Conservancy\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Greenbrier" title="The Greenbrier">\n        The Greenbrier\n       </a>\n       hotel and\n       <a href="/wiki/Resort" title="Resort">\n        resort\n       </a>\n       , originally built in 1778, has long been considered a premier hotel, frequented by numerous world leaders and U.S. presidents over the years.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia is the site of the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Radio_Astronomy_Observatory" title="National Radio Astronomy Observatory">\n        National Radio Astronomy Observatory\n       </a>\n       , which features the\n       <a href="/wiki/Green_Bank_Telescope" title="Green Bank Telescope">\n        Green Bank Telescope\n       </a>\n       . The main building of\n       <a href="/wiki/Trans-Allegheny_Lunatic_Asylum" title="Trans-Allegheny Lunatic Asylum">\n        Weston State Hospital\n       </a>\n       is the largest hand-cut sandstone building in the western hemisphere, second worldwide only to the Kremlin in Moscow.\n       <a href="/wiki/Tours" title="Tours">\n        Tours\n       </a>\n       of the building, which is a\n       <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Landmark" title="National Historic Landmark">\n        National Historic Landmark\n       </a>\n       and part of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Civil_War_Discovery_Trail" title="Civil War Discovery Trail">\n        National Civil War Trail\n       </a>\n       , are offered seasonally and by appointment year round. West Virginia has numerous popular festivals throughout the year.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG/220px-WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG/330px-WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG/440px-WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennial.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         WV State Sesquicentennial\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Resources">\n        Resources\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Resources">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coalseam_8618.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="400" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Coalseam_8618.JPG/220px-Coalseam_8618.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Coalseam_8618.JPG/330px-Coalseam_8618.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/08/Coalseam_8618.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coalseam_8618.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Bituminous coal seam in southwestern West Virginia\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       One of the major resources in West Virginia\'s economy is\n       <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">\n        coal\n       </a>\n       . According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">\n        Energy Information Administration\n       </a>\n       , West Virginia is a top coal-producer in the United States, second only to Wyoming. West Virginia is located in the heart of the Marcellus Shale Natural Gas Bed, which stretches from Tennessee north to New York in the middle of Appalachia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Nearly all of the electricity generated in West Virginia is from coal-fired power plants. West Virginia produces a surplus of electricity and leads the Nation in net interstate electricity exports.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Farming is also practiced in West Virginia, but on a limited basis because of the mountainous terrain over much of the state.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Green_energy">\n        Green energy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Green energy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia has the potential to generate 4,952 GWh/year from 1,883 MW of wind power, using 80 meter high wind turbines, or 8,627 GWh/year from 2,772 MW of 100 meter wind turbines, and 60,000 GWh from 40,000 MW of photovoltaics, including 3,810 MW of rooftop photovoltaics.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Taxes">\n        Taxes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Taxes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia personal\n       <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">\n        income tax\n       </a>\n       is based on federal adjusted gross income (not taxable income), as modified by specific items in West Virginia law. Citizens are taxed within five income brackets, which range from 3.0 percent to 6.5 percent. The state\'s consumer\n       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">\n        sales tax\n       </a>\n       is levied at 6 percent. Effective January 1, 2004, calculation of WV consumer sales tax has been converted to a calculated figure from the bracket system, and remains at 6 percent for most goods (non-prepared foods are not taxed\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia counties administer and collect\n       <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">\n        property taxes\n       </a>\n       , although property tax rates reflect levies for state government, county governments, county boards of education and municipalities. Counties may also impose a hotel occupancy tax on lodging places not located within the city limits of any municipality that levies such a tax. Municipalities may levy license and\n       <a href="/wiki/Gross_receipts_tax" title="Gross receipts tax">\n        gross receipts taxes\n       </a>\n       on businesses located within the city limits and a hotel occupancy tax on lodging places in the city. Although the Department of Tax and Revenue plays a major role in the administration of this tax, less than one-half of 1 percent of the property tax collected goes to state government.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The primary beneficiaries of the property tax are county boards of education. Property taxes are paid to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Sheriffs_in_the_United_States" title="Sheriffs in the United States">\n        sheriff\n       </a>\n       of each of the state\'s 55 counties. Each county and municipality can impose its own rates of property taxation within the limits set by the West Virginia Constitution. The West Virginia legislature sets the rate of tax of county boards of education. This rate is used by all county boards of education statewide. However, the total tax rate for county boards of education may differ from county to county because of excess levies. The Department of Tax and Revenue supervises and otherwise assists counties and municipalities in their work of assessment and tax rate determination. The total tax rate is a combination of the tax levies from four state taxing authorities: state, county, schools and municipal. This total tax rate varies for each of the four classes of property, which consists of personal, real and intangible properties. Property is assessed according to its use, location and value as of July 1. All property is reappraised every three years; annual adjustments are made to assessments for property with a change of value. West Virginia does not impose an\n       <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">\n        inheritance tax\n       </a>\n       . Because of the phase-out of the federal\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estate_tax" title="Estate tax">\n        estate tax\n       </a>\n       credit, West Virginia\'s estate tax is not imposed on estates of persons who died on or after January 1, 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_private_employers">\n        Largest private employers\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span World">\n          Tudor\'s Biscuit World\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         49\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Weirton Medical Center\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         50\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcan_Rolled_Products" title="Alcan Rolled Products">\n          Alcan Rolled Products\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Quality_of_life">\n        Quality of life\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Quality of life">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bluefield,_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3153" data-file-width="2048" height="339" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bluefield%2C_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg/220px-Bluefield%2C_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bluefield%2C_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg/330px-Bluefield%2C_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Bluefield%2C_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg/440px-Bluefield%2C_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bluefield,_West_Virginia_-_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/Bluefield,_West_Virginia" title="Bluefield, West Virginia">\n          Bluefield\n         </a>\n         in 2014\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-too_few_opinions" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          The examples and perspective in this article\n          <b>\n           may not\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">\n            include all significant viewpoints\n           </a>\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           Please\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit">\n            improve the article\n           </a>\n           or\n           <a href="/wiki/Talk:West_Virginia" title="Talk:West Virginia">\n            discuss the issue\n           </a>\n           .\n          </span>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (February 2016)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_2">\n        Economy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia Governor Tomblin\'s proposed 2014\xe2\x80\x9315 budget submitted in January 2014 had an estimated budget gap of $146\xe2\x80\x93$265 million, and halfway through the 2013\xe2\x80\x9314 fiscal year, tax revenues were $82 million short.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The West Virginia Legislature in March 2014 passed its budget bill, taking $147 million from the Rainy Day Fund to balance the 2015 budget.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Governor Tomblin\'s Deputy Chief of Staff Jason Pizatella, after the state legislature passed the budget, said that West Virginia is expecting another dismal budget in 2016 and could need $150\xe2\x80\x93170 million to balance the next year\'s budget.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">\n        <a href="#cite_note-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia coal exports declined 40% in 2013 \xe2\x80\x93 a loss of $2.9 billion and overall total exports declined 26%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">\n        <a href="#cite_note-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia ranked last in the Gallup Economic Index for the fourth year running. West Virginia\'s score was \xe2\x88\x9244, or a full 17 points lower than the average of \xe2\x88\x9227 for the other states in the bottom ten.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">\n        <a href="#cite_note-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia ranked 48th in the CNBC "Top States for Business 2013" based on measures of competitiveness such as economy, workforce and cost of living \xe2\x80\x93 ranking among the bottom 5 states for the last six years running.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n        <a href="#cite_note-101">\n         [101]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia ranked 49th in the 2014 State New Economy Index, and has ranked in the bottom three states since 1999. West Virginia ranked last or next-to-last in critical indicators such as Workforce Education, Entrepreneurial Activity, High-Tech Jobs, and Scientists and Engineers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n        <a href="#cite_note-102">\n         [102]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On January 9, 2014 near Charleston, the state capital, a\n       <a href="/wiki/2014_Elk_River_chemical_spill" title="2014 Elk River chemical spill">\n        chemical spill\n       </a>\n       occurred that contaminated the water supply of 300,000 people in nine West Virginia counties. According to Bloomberg News, lost wages, revenue, and other economic harm from the chemical spill could top $500 million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and West Virginia\'s Marshall University Center for Business and Economic Research estimated that about $61 million was lost by businesses in the first four days alone after the spill.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Employment">\n        Employment\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Employment">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 2012, West Virginia\'s Gross Domestic Product (GDP) grew by 3.3%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state issued a report highlighting the state\'s GDP as indicating a fast-growing economy, but did not address employment indicators.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2009\xe2\x80\x932013, the U.S. real GDP increased 9.6% and total employment increased 3.9%. In West Virginia during the same time period, its real GDP increased about 11%, while total employment decreased by 1,000 jobs from 746,000 to 745,000.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2013, West Virginia ranked last in the nation with an\n       <a href="/wiki/Employment-to-population_ratio" title="Employment-to-population ratio">\n        employment-to-population ratio\n       </a>\n       of only 50%, compared to the national average of 59%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state lost 5,600 jobs in its labor force in four critical economic sectors: construction (1,900), manufacturing (1,100), retail (1,800), and education (800), while gaining just 400 in mining and logging.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The state\'s Civilian Labor Force dropped by 15,100.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">\n        <a href="#cite_note-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Wages">\n        Wages\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Wages">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Personal income growth in West Virginia during 2013 was only 1.5% \xe2\x80\x93 the lowest in the nation \xe2\x80\x93 and about half the national average of 2.6%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">\n        <a href="#cite_note-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Overall income growth in West Virginia in the last 30 years has been only 13% (about one-third of the national average of 37%). Wages of the impoverished bottom 1% income earners decreased by 3%, compared to the national average, which increased 19%.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Population">\n        Population\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Population">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       United Van Lines 37th Annual Migration Study showed in 2013 that 60% more people moved out of the Mountain State than moved in.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia\'s population is expected to decline by more than 19,000 residents by 2030, and West Virginia could lose one of its three seats in the United States House of Representatives.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n        <a href="#cite_note-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       West Virginia is the only state where death rates exceeds birth rates. During 2010\xe2\x80\x932013, about 21,000 babies per year were born in West Virginia, but over 3 years West Virginia had 3,000 more deaths than births.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_114-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census1-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Family">\n        Family\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Family">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Gallup-Healthways annual "State of American Well-Being" rankings reports that 1,261 concerned West Virginians rated themselves as "suffering" in categories such as Quality of Life, Physical Health, and Access to Basic Needs. Overall, West Virginia citizens rated themselves as being more miserable than people in all other states \xe2\x80\x93 for 5 years running.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition, the Gallup Well-Being Index for 2013 ranked Charleston, the state capital, and Huntington last and next-to-last out of 189 U.S. Metropolitan Statistical Areas.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Annie E. Casey Foundation\'s National Index of Children\'s Progress ranked West Virginia 43rd in the nation for all kids, and last for white kids.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n        <a href="#cite_note-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Annie E. Casey Foundation\'s 2013 KIDS COUNT Data Book also ranked West Virginia\'s education system 47th in the nation for the second straight year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Charleston, West Virginia has the worst divorce rate among 100 cities in the nation. Stephen Smith, the executive director of the West Virginia Healthy Kids and Families Coalition, said that poor employment prospects are to blame: "The pressure to make a good living puts strain on a marriage, and right now it is infinitely harder to make a living here than it was 40 years ago."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Health">\n        Health\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Health">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       United Health Foundation\'s "America\'s Health Rankings" for 2013 found that Americans are making considerable progress in key health measures. West Virginia, however, ranked either last or second-to-last in 20 categories, including cancer, child immunization, diabetes, disabilities, drug deaths, teeth loss, low birth weight, missed work days due to health, prescription drug overdose, preventable hospitalizations, and senior clinical care.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Wisconsin Population Health Institute annual "Health Rankings" for 2012 showed West Virginia spends $9,671 per capita on health care annually. El Salvador spends just $467, yet both have the same life expectancy.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2012, according to the Census Bureau, West Virginia was the only state where death rates exceeds birth rates. During 2010\xe2\x80\x932013, about 21,000 babies per year were born in West Virginia, but there were 24,000 deaths.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census1_114-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-census1-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In demographics, this is called a "net mortality society."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The National Center for Health Statistics says that national birth rates for teenagers are at historic lows \xe2\x80\x93 during 2007\xe2\x80\x932010, teen birth rates fell 17% nationally;. West Virginia, however, ranked last with a 3% increase in birth rates for teenagers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A study by West Virginia\'s Marshall University showed that 19% of babies born in the state have evidence of drug or alcohol exposure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This is several times the national rate, where studies show that about 5.9% of pregnant women in the U.S. use illicit drugs, and about 8.5% consume any alcohol.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An Institute for Health Policy Research study determined that mortality rates in Appalachia are correlated with coal production. In twenty West Virginia coal counties mining more than 1 million tons of coal per year and having a total population of 850,000, there are about 10,100 deaths per year, with 1,400 of those statistically attributed to deaths from heart, respiratory and kidney disease from living in an Appalachian coal county.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 2015,\n       <a href="/wiki/McDowell_County,_West_Virginia" title="McDowell County, West Virginia">\n        McDowell County\n       </a>\n       had the highest rate of drug-induced deaths of any county in the United States, with a rate of 141 deaths per 100,000 people. Four of the five US counties with the highest rates of drug-induced deaths are located in West Virginia (McDowell, Wyoming, Cabell and Raleigh Counties).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">\n        Governance\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Governance">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Law_and_government_of_West_Virginia" title="Law and government of West Virginia">\n        Law and government of West Virginia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Constitution" title="West Virginia Constitution">\n        West Virginia Constitution\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WV_State_Capitol.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/WV_State_Capitol.jpg/220px-WV_State_Capitol.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/WV_State_Capitol.jpg/330px-WV_State_Capitol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/WV_State_Capitol.jpg/440px-WV_State_Capitol.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WV_State_Capitol.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The West Virginia State Capitol.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG/220px-South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG/330px-South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG/440px-South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:South_Side_WV_State_Capitol_Sesquicentennia.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         150th Statehood\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia\'s capital and seat of government is the city of\n       <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_West_Virginia" title="Charleston, West Virginia">\n        Charleston\n       </a>\n       , located in the southwest area of the state.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">\n        Legislative branch\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Legislative branch">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Legislature" title="West Virginia Legislature">\n        West Virginia Legislature\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The West Virginia Legislature is\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">\n        bicameral\n       </a>\n       . It consists of the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_House_of_Delegates" title="West Virginia House of Delegates">\n        House of Delegates\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Senate" title="West Virginia Senate">\n        Senate\n       </a>\n       . It is a citizen\'s legislature, meaning that legislative office is not a full-time occupation, but rather a part-time position. Consequently, the legislators often hold a full-time job in their community of residence.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Typically, the legislature is in session for 60 days between January and early April. The final day of the regular session ends in a bewildering fury of last-minute legislation to meet a constitutionally imposed midnight deadline. During the remainder of the year, monthly interim sessions are held in preparation for the regular session. Legislators also gather periodically for \'special\' sessions when called by the governor.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The title of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant governor (United States)">\n        Lieutenant Governor\n       </a>\n       is assigned by statute to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_West_Virginia" title="Lieutenant Governor of West Virginia">\n        Senate President\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">\n        Executive branch\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Executive branch">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors_of_West_Virginia" title="List of Governors of West Virginia">\n        List of Governors of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The governor, elected every four years on the same day as the U.S. Presidential election, is sworn in during the following January.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Governors of West Virginia can serve two consecutive terms but must sit out a term before serving a third term in office.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The title of\n       <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_governor_(United_States)" title="Lieutenant governor (United States)">\n        Lieutenant Governor\n       </a>\n       is assigned by statute to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_West_Virginia" title="Lieutenant Governor of West Virginia">\n        Senate President\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">\n        Judicial branch\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Judicial branch">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Appeals_of_West_Virginia" title="Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia">\n        Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia is one of nineteen states that do not have a\n       <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment_in_the_United_States" title="Capital punishment in the United States">\n        death penalty\n       </a>\n       , and it is the only state in the southeastern United States to have abolished it.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For the purpose of courts of general jurisdiction, the state is divided into 31 judicial circuits. Each circuit is made up of one or more counties. Circuit judges are elected in partisan elections to serve eight-year terms.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia\'s highest court is the Supreme Court of Appeals. The Supreme Court of Appeals of West Virginia is the busiest appellate court of its type in the United States. West Virginia is one of 11 states with a single appellate court. The state constitution allows for the creation of an intermediate court of appeals, but the Legislature has never created one. The Supreme Court is made up of five justices, elected in non-partisan elections to 12-year terms.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia is an\n       <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage_control_state" title="Alcoholic beverage control state">\n        alcoholic beverage control state\n       </a>\n       . However, unlike most such states, it does not operate retail outlets, having exited that business in 1990. It retains a monopoly on wholesaling of\n       <a href="/wiki/Distilled_beverage" title="Distilled beverage">\n        distilled spirits\n       </a>\n       only.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">\n        Politics\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Politics">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_West_Virginia" title="Elections in West Virginia">\n        Elections in West Virginia\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_West_Virginia" title="Political party strength in West Virginia">\n        Political party strength in West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Original_research" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n background:#fff3f3;">\n         32.06%\n         <i>\n          253,953\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#f0f0ff;">\n         <b>\n          67.94%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          538,087\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#f0f0ff;">\n         <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1960" title="United States presidential election, 1960">\n          1960\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#fff3f3;">\n         47.27%\n         <i>\n          395,995\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td style="text-align:center; background:#f0f0ff;">\n         <b>\n          52.73%\n         </b>\n         <i>\n          441,786\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       At the state level, West Virginia\'s politics were largely dominated by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">\n        Democratic Party\n       </a>\n       from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">\n        Great Depression\n       </a>\n       through the 2000s. This was a legacy of West Virginia\'s very strong tradition of union membership.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slate.com_129-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-slate.com-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since 2000, state elections have become more competitive at both the state and federal levels. After the 2014 midterm elections, Democrats controlled the governorship, the majority of statewide offices, and one U.S. Senate seat, while Republicans held one U.S. Senate seat, all three of the state\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._House" title="U.S. House">\n        U.S. House\n       </a>\n       seats, and a majority in both houses of the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Legislature" title="West Virginia Legislature">\n        West Virginia Legislature\n       </a>\n       . In the 2016 elections, the Republicans held on to their seats and made gains in the State Senate and gained three statewide offices.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2000_US_Presidential_Election" title="2000 US Presidential Election">\n        2000\n       </a>\n       , West Virginians have supported the Republican candidate in every presidential election. The state is regarded as a\n       <a href="/wiki/Red_states_and_blue_states" title="Red states and blue states">\n        "deep red"\n       </a>\n       state at the federal level.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slate.com_129-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-slate.com-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_US_Presidential_Election" title="2012 US Presidential Election">\n        2012 presidential election\n       </a>\n       Republican\n       <a href="/wiki/Mitt_Romney" title="Mitt Romney">\n        Mitt Romney\n       </a>\n       won the state defeating Democrat\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       with 62% of the vote to 35% for Obama. In the 2016 presidential election, Republican\n       <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">\n        Donald Trump\n       </a>\n       won the state with 67.86% of the popular vote, with West Virginia being the second-highest percentage voting for Trump of any state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leip.2C_David_128-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Leip.2C_David-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Before 2000, West Virginia had been reckoned as a Democratic stronghold at the national level. From 1932 to 1996, the state voted in favor of the Republican Party three times\xe2\x80\x94in the national Republican landslides of 1956, 1972 and 1984.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Evangelical Christians comprised 52 percent of the state\'s voters in 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A poll in 2005 showed that 53 percent of West Virginia voters are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pro-life" title="Pro-life">\n        pro-life\n       </a>\n       , the seventh highest in the country.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A September 2011\n       <a href="/wiki/Public_Policy_Polling" title="Public Policy Polling">\n        Public Policy Polling\n       </a>\n       survey found that 19% of West Virginia voters thought that same-sex marriage should be legal, while 71% thought it should be illegal and 10% were not sure. A separate question on the same survey found that 43% of West Virginia voters supported the legal recognition of same-sex couples, with 17% supporting same-sex marriage, 26% supporting civil unions but not marriage, 54% favoring no legal recognition and 3% not sure.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2008, 58 percent favored troop withdrawal from Iraq while just 32 percent wanted troops to remain.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On fiscal policy in 2008, 52 percent said raising taxes on the wealthier individuals would benefit the economy, while 45 percent disagreed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">\n        Transportation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transportation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WVtollbooth.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/WVtollbooth.jpg/220px-WVtollbooth.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/WVtollbooth.jpg/330px-WVtollbooth.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/WVtollbooth.jpg/440px-WVtollbooth.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WVtollbooth.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A toll plaza on the\n         <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Turnpike" title="West Virginia Turnpike">\n          West Virginia Turnpike\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2470" data-file-width="3648" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg/220px-View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg/330px-View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg/440px-View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:View_of_New_River_Gorge_Bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         View of the iconic\n         <a href="/wiki/New_River_Gorge_Bridge" title="New River Gorge Bridge">\n          New River Gorge Bridge\n         </a>\n         from the overlook at the north end of the New River Gorge (facing southwards), near\n         <a href="/wiki/Fayetteville,_West_Virginia" title="Fayetteville, West Virginia">\n          Fayetteville\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg/220px-Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg/330px-Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg/440px-Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Weirton-Steubenville_Bridge_pic_1.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/Veterans_Memorial_Bridge_(Steubenville,_Ohio)" title="Veterans Memorial Bridge (Steubenville, Ohio)">\n          Veterans Memorial Bridge\n         </a>\n         carries US 22 between Weirton and Steubenville, Ohio. It is similar in design to the new bridge connecting\n         <a href="/wiki/Proctorville,_Ohio" title="Proctorville, Ohio">\n          Proctorville, Ohio\n         </a>\n         (Ohio Rt 7) with\n         <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_West_Virginia" title="Huntington, West Virginia">\n          Huntington, West Virginia\n         </a>\n         via US 60.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_West_Virginia" title="Transportation in West Virginia">\n        Transportation in West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Highways form the backbone of transportation systems in West Virginia, with over 37,300 miles (60,000\xc2\xa0km) of public roads in the state.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Airports, railroads, and rivers complete the commercial transportation modes for West Virginia. Commercial air travel is facilitated by airports in Charleston, Huntington, Morgantown, Beckley, Lewisburg, Clarksburg, and Parkersburg. All but Charleston and Huntington are subsidized by the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Transportation" title="United States Department of Transportation">\n        US Department of Transportation\'s\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Essential_Air_Service" title="Essential Air Service">\n        Essential Air Service\n       </a>\n       program. The cities of Charleston, Huntington, Beckley, Wheeling, Morgantown, Clarksburg, Parkersburg and Fairmont have bus-based public transit systems, and the Huntington and Charleston systems jointly operate a twice per weekday interconnecting service.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_University" title="West Virginia University">\n        West Virginia University\n       </a>\n       in Morgantown boasts the\n       <a href="/wiki/Morgantown_Personal_Rapid_Transit" title="Morgantown Personal Rapid Transit">\n        PRT (personal rapid transit) system\n       </a>\n       , the state\'s only single rail public transit system. Developed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">\n        Boeing\n       </a>\n       , the WVU School of Engineering and the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Transportation" title="United States Department of Transportation">\n        Department of Transportation\n       </a>\n       , it was a model for low-capacity light transport designed for smaller cities. Recreational transportation opportunities abound in West Virginia, including hiking trails,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_trails" title="Rail trails">\n        rail trails\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">\n        <a href="#cite_note-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ATV off-road trails,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">\n        <a href="#cite_note-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       white water rafting rivers,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">\n        <a href="#cite_note-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and two tourist railroads, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cass_Scenic_Railroad" title="Cass Scenic Railroad">\n        Cass Scenic Railroad\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">\n        <a href="#cite_note-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/South_Branch_Valley_Railroad" title="South Branch Valley Railroad">\n        Potomac Eagle Scenic Railroad\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">\n        <a href="#cite_note-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia is crossed by six\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstate_highways" title="Interstate highways">\n        interstate highways\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64" title="Interstate 64">\n        I-64\n       </a>\n       enters the state near\n       <a href="/wiki/White_Sulphur_Springs,_West_Virginia" title="White Sulphur Springs, West Virginia">\n        White Sulphur Springs\n       </a>\n       in the mountainous east, and exits for\n       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">\n        Kentucky\n       </a>\n       in the west, near\n       <a href="/wiki/Huntington,_West_Virginia" title="Huntington, West Virginia">\n        Huntington\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_77" title="Interstate 77">\n        I-77\n       </a>\n       enters from\n       <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">\n        Virginia\n       </a>\n       in the south, near\n       <a href="/wiki/Bluefield,_West_Virginia" title="Bluefield, West Virginia">\n        Bluefield\n       </a>\n       . It runs north past\n       <a href="/wiki/Parkersburg,_West_Virginia" title="Parkersburg, West Virginia">\n        Parkersburg\n       </a>\n       before it crosses into\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">\n        Ohio\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_64" title="Interstate 64">\n        I-64\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_77" title="Interstate 77">\n        I-77\n       </a>\n       between Charleston and Beckley are merged as toll road known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Turnpike" title="West Virginia Turnpike">\n        West Virginia Turnpike\n       </a>\n       , which continues as I-77 alone from Beckley to Princeton. It was constructed beginning in 1952 as a two lane road, but rebuilt beginning in 1974 to interstate standards. Today almost nothing of the original construction remains.\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_68" title="Interstate 68">\n        I-68\n       </a>\n       \'s western terminus is in\n       <a href="/wiki/Morgantown,_West_Virginia" title="Morgantown, West Virginia">\n        Morgantown\n       </a>\n       . From there it runs east into\n       <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">\n        Maryland\n       </a>\n       . At the\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_68" title="Interstate 68">\n        I-68\n       </a>\n       terminus in Morgantown, it meets\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_79" title="Interstate 79">\n        I-79\n       </a>\n       , which enters from Pennsylvania and runs through the state to its southern terminus in\n       <a href="/wiki/Charleston,_West_Virginia" title="Charleston, West Virginia">\n        Charleston\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70" title="Interstate 70">\n        I-70\n       </a>\n       briefly runs through West Virginia, crossing the northern panhandle through\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheeling,_West_Virginia" title="Wheeling, West Virginia">\n        Wheeling\n       </a>\n       , while\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_470_(Ohio%E2%80%93West_Virginia)" title="Interstate 470 (Ohio\xe2\x80\x93West Virginia)">\n        I-470\n       </a>\n       is a bypass of Wheeling (making Wheeling among the smallest cities with an interstate bypass).\n       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_81" title="Interstate 81">\n        I-81\n       </a>\n       also briefly runs in West Virginia through the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Panhandle" title="Eastern Panhandle">\n        Eastern Panhandle\n       </a>\n       where it goes through\n       <a href="/wiki/Martinsburg,_West_Virginia" title="Martinsburg, West Virginia">\n        Martinsburg\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The interstates are supplemented by roads constructed under the Appalachian Corridor system. Four Corridors are complete. Corridor D, carrying US 50, runs from the Ohio River, and I-77, at Parkersburg to I-79 at Clarksburg. Corridor G, carrying US 119, runs from Charleston to the Kentucky border at Williamson. Corridor L, carrying US 19, runs from the Turnpike at Beckley to I-79 near Sutton (and provides a short cut of about 40 miles and bypasses Charleston\'s urban traffic for traveler heading to and from Florida). Corridor Q, carrying US 460, runs through Mercer County, entering the state from\n       <a href="/wiki/Giles_County,_Virginia" title="Giles County, Virginia">\n        Giles County, Virginia\n       </a>\n       and then reentering Virginia at\n       <a href="/wiki/Tazewell_County,_Virginia" title="Tazewell County, Virginia">\n        Tazewell County\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Work continues on the long delayed Corridor H, which will carry US 48 from Weston to the Virginia line near Wardensville. As of 2013, a section from Weston to Elkins, and another section from Wardensville to near Scher are complete. Other projects under development are a four-lane upgrade of US 35 from Scott Depot to the Ohio River at Point Pleasant, which is about two-thirds complete; a four lane upgrade of WV 10 from Logan to Man and then of WV 80 from Man to Gilbert, which is about one-third complete; and four lane upgrades to US 52 from Bluefield to Williamson, known as the "King Coal Highway" and from Williamson to Huntington, known as the "Tolsia Highway" which are many years from completion. A project known as the "Coalfields Expressway" is also ongoing, and will carry US 121 from Beckley west across Raleigh, Wyoming, and McDowell counties, entering Virginia near Bishop.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rail lines in the state used to be more prevalent, but many lines have been discontinued because of increased automobile traffic. Many old tracks have been converted to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rail_trails" title="Rail trails">\n        rail trails\n       </a>\n       for recreational use, although the coal producing areas still have railroads running at near capacity.\n       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">\n        Amtrak\n       </a>\n       \'s Cardinal roughly parallels I-64\'s path through the state.\n       <a href="/wiki/MARC_Train" title="MARC Train">\n        MARC\n       </a>\n       trains serve commuters in the eastern panhandle. In 2006\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" title="Norfolk Southern">\n        Norfolk Southern\n       </a>\n       along with the West Virginia and U.S. Government approved a plan to modify many of the rail tunnels in West Virginia, especially in the southern half of the state, to allow for double stacked cars (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Intermodal_freight_transport" title="Intermodal freight transport">\n        inter-modal freight\n       </a>\n       ). This is expected to also help bring economic growth to the southern half of the state. An Intermodal Freight Facility is under construction near Prichard, south of Huntington.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Because of the mountainous nature of the entire state, West Virginia has several notable tunnels and bridges. The most famous of these is the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_River_Gorge_Bridge" title="New River Gorge Bridge">\n        New River Gorge Bridge\n       </a>\n       , which was at a time the longest steel single-arch bridge in the world with a 3,031-foot (924\xc2\xa0m) span. The bridge is also pictured on the West Virginia\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_quarter" title="State quarter">\n        state quarter\n       </a>\n       . The Fort Steuben Bridge (Weirton-Steubenville Bridge) was at its time of construction one of only three cable-stayed steel girder trusses in the United States. "The Veterans Memorial Bridge was designed to handle traffic from the Fort Steuben Bridge as well as its own traffic load", to quote the\n       <i>\n        Weirton Daily Times\n       </i>\n       newspaper.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gossett_Fort_Steuben_Bridge_permanently_closed_145-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Gossett_Fort_Steuben_Bridge_permanently_closed-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The 80-year-old Fort Steuben Bridge (Weirton-Steubenville Bridge) was permanently closed on January 8, 2009. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheeling_Suspension_Bridge" title="Wheeling Suspension Bridge">\n        Wheeling Suspension Bridge\n       </a>\n       was the first bridge built across the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">\n        Ohio River\n       </a>\n       in 1849 and for a time was the longest suspension bridge in the world. It is still the oldest vehicular suspension bridge in the United States still in use.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Important_cities_and_towns">\n        Important cities and towns\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a city\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image"
