   </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="State_capitals">\n        State capitals\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: State capitals">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Originally, the state capital was in Wheeling (1863 to 1870). It was then moved to Charleston, a more central city (1870 to 1875). However it was returned to Wheeling in 1875, until the capitol burned down in 1885. It was moved back to Charleston in 1885, and it has been there since.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">\n        <a href="#cite_note-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Large_cities">\n        Large cities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span    </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table border="0">\n       <tr>\n        <td valign="top">\n         <ul>\n  </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Towns_and_small_cities">\n        Towns and small cities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Towns and small cities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <table border="0">\n       <tr>\n        <td valign="top">\n         <ul>\n          <li>\n           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bath_(Berkeley_Springs),_West_Virginia" title="Bath (Berkeley Springs), West Virginia">\n            Berkeley Springs\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Bridgeport,_West_Virginia" title="Bridgeport, West Virginia">\n            Bridgeport\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a href="/wiki/Buckhannon,_West_Virginia" title="Buckhannon, West Virginia">\n            Buckhannon\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li>\n           <a class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Culture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">\n        Sports\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Sports">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia is home to college sports teams from two schools \xe2\x80\x93 West Virginia and Marshall \xe2\x80\x93 that play in NCAA Division I. West Virginia is also home to several professional minor league baseball, football, soccer, and other sports teams.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <a title="Ice hockey">\n          Ice hockey\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/ECHL" title="ECHL">\n          ECHL\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association_(2000%E2%80%93present)" title="American Basketball Association (2000\xe2\x80\x93present)">\n          American Basketball Association (2000\xe2\x80\x93present)\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         West Virginia Lightning\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">\n          <a href="#cite_note-148">\n           [148]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">\n          Football\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Elite Mid-Continental Football League\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149">\n          <a href="#cite_note-149">\n           [149]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Chaos" title="West Virginia Chaos">\n          West Virginia Chaos\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer">\n          Soccer\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Bruisers" title="West Virginia Bruisers">\n          West Virginia Bruisers\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">\n          Football\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Football_Alliance" title="Women\'s Football Alliance">\n          Women\'s Football Alliance\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">\n        Music\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Music">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_West_Virginia" title="Music of West Virginia">\n        Music of West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Appalachian_music">\n        Appalachian music\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Appalachian music">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       West Virginia\'s folk heritage is a part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appalachian_folk_music" title="Appalachian folk music">\n        Appalachian folk music\n       </a>\n       tradition, and includes styles of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musical_styles_(violin)#Fiddle" title="Musical styles (violin)">\n        fiddling\n       </a>\n       , ballad singing, and other styles that draw on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ulster-Scots" title="Ulster-Scots">\n        Scots-Irish\n       </a>\n       music. Camp Washington-Carver, a Mountain Cultural Arts Center located at\n       <a href="/wiki/Clifftop,_Fayette_County,_West_Virginia" title="Clifftop, Fayette County, West Virginia">\n        Clifftop\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Fayette_County,_West_Virginia" title="Fayette County, West Virginia">\n        Fayette County\n       </a>\n       , hosts an annual Appalachian String Band Festival.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Capitol Complex in Charleston hosts The Vandalia Gathering, where traditional Appalachian musicians compete in contests and play in impromptu jam sessions and evening concerts over the course of the weekend.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Augusta Heritage Center sponsored by Davis &amp; Elkins College in\n       <a href="/wiki/Elkins,_West_Virginia" title="Elkins, West Virginia">\n        Elkins\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Randolph_County,_West_Virginia" title="Randolph County, West Virginia">\n        Randolph County\n       </a>\n       produces the annual\n       <a href="/wiki/Augusta_Heritage_Festival" title="Augusta Heritage Festival">\n        Augusta Heritage Festival\n       </a>\n       , which includes intensive week-long workshops in the summer that help preserve Appalachian heritage and traditions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classical_music">\n        Classical music\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Classical music">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The West Virginia Symphony Orchestra was founded in 1939, as the\n       <i>\n        Charleston Civic Orchestra\n       </i>\n       , before becoming the\n       <i>\n        Charleston Symphony Orchestra\n       </i>\n       in 1943. The first conductor was William R. Wiant, followed by the conductor Antonio Modarelli, who was written about in the November 7, 1949\n       <i>\n        Time Magazine\n       </i>\n       for his composition of the\n       <i>\n        River Saga\n       </i>\n       , a six-section program piece about the Kanawha River according to the\n       <i>\n        Charleston Gazette\n       </i>\n       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\n        \'\n       </span>\n       s November 6, 1999 photo essay, "Snapshots of the 20th Century".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153">\n        <a href="#cite_note-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Before coming to Charleston, Modarelli had conducted the\n       <a href="/wiki/Wheeling_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Wheeling Symphony Orchestra">\n        Wheeling Symphony Orchestra\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_Orchestra" title="Philadelphia Orchestra">\n        Philadelphia Orchestra\n       </a>\n       , according to the orchestra\'s website.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n        <a href="#cite_note-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">\n        Pulitzer Prize\n       </a>\n       -winning 20th-century composer\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Crumb" title="George Crumb">\n        George Crumb\n       </a>\n       was born in Charleston and earned his bachelor\'s degree there before moving outside the state. There had also been a series of operatic style concerts performed in Wheeling during mid-century as well.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_innovation">\n        Musical innovation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Musical innovation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The West Virginia Cultural Center in Charleston\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155">\n        <a href="#cite_note-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is home to the West Virginia Division of Culture and History,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">\n        <a href="#cite_note-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which helps underwrite and coordinate a large number of musical activities. The center is also home to\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Stage" title="Mountain Stage">\n         Mountain Stage\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , an internationally broadcast live-performance music radio program established in 1983 that is carried by many affiliates of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio">\n        National Public Radio\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n        <a href="#cite_note-157">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The program also travels to other venues in the state such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_University" title="West Virginia University">\n        West Virginia University\n       </a>\n       Creative Arts Center in Morgantown.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n        <a href="#cite_note-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The center hosts concerts sponsored by the Friends of Old Time Music and Dance, which brings an assortment of acoustic roots music to West Virginians.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The center also hosts the West Virginia Dance Festival, which features classical and modern dance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">\n        <a href="#cite_note-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Huntington\'s historic\n       <a href="/wiki/Keith-Albee_Theatre" title="Keith-Albee Theatre">\n        Keith-Albee Theatre\n       </a>\n       , built by brothers A.B. and S.J. Hyman, was originally opened to the public on May 7, 1928, and hosts a variety of performing arts and music attractions. The theatre was eventually gifted to\n       <a href="/wiki/Marshall_University" title="Marshall University">\n        Marshall University\n       </a>\n       and is currently going through renovation to restore it to its original splendor.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Every summer\n       <a href="/wiki/Elkins,_West_Virginia" title="Elkins, West Virginia">\n        Elkins\n       </a>\n       hosts the Augusta Heritage Festival, which brings folk musicians from around the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">\n        <a href="#cite_note-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The town of\n       <a href="/wiki/Glenville,_West_Virginia" title="Glenville, West Virginia">\n        Glenville\n       </a>\n       has long been home to the annual West Virginia State Folk Festival.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">\n        <a href="#cite_note-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Mountaineer Opera House in\n       <a href="/wiki/Milton,_West_Virginia" title="Milton, West Virginia">\n        Milton\n       </a>\n       hosts a variety of musical acts.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       John Denver\'s hit song "\n       <a href="/wiki/Take_Me_Home,_Country_Roads" title="Take Me Home, Country Roads">\n        Take Me Home, Country Roads\n       </a>\n       " describes the experience of driving through West Virginia. The song mentions the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shenandoah_River" title="Shenandoah River">\n        Shenandoah River\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Blue_Ridge_Mountains" title="Blue Ridge Mountains">\n        Blue Ridge Mountains\n       </a>\n       , both features traversing the easternmost extremity of the state\'s "eastern panhandle", in\n       <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_West_Virginia" title="Jefferson County, West Virginia">\n        Jefferson County\n       </a>\n       . On March 8, 2014, West Virginia Governor Earl Ray Tomblin signed House Concurrent Resolution 40 naming "Take Me Home, Country Roads" the fourth official state song of West Virginia.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Symphony Sunday is an annual event hosted by the\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Symphony_Orchestra" title="West Virginia Symphony Orchestra">\n        West Virginia Symphony Orchestra\n       </a>\n       held in June. It is a day full day of music by community groups, food, and family fun, culminating in a free performance by the West Virginia Symphony Orchestra with a fireworks display following. The event began in 1982 and is held on the front lawn of the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Charleston" title="University of Charleston">\n        University of Charleston\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Daily_Mail_Kanawha_County_Majorette_and_Band_Festival" title="Daily Mail Kanawha County Majorette and Band Festival">\n        Daily Mail Kanawha County Majorette and Band Festival\n       </a>\n       is West Virginia\'s longest running music festival. It is for the eight public high schools in Kanawha County. The festival began in 1947. It is held at the\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Charleston_Stadium_at_Laidley_Field" title="University of Charleston Stadium at Laidley Field">\n        University of Charleston Stadium at Laidley Field\n       </a>\n       in downtown Charleston.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">\n        Literature\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Literature">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_literature" title="West Virginia literature">\n        West Virginia literature\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">\n        In popular culture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=West_Virginia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: In popular culture">\n West Virginia\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span
